Chen Shaokuan

Discusses Surveying and Disaster Relief

First, Complete the Survey of the Jiangyin-Wusong Section

Flood Victims Flee Inland, Warships Unable to Provide Assistance

Chen Shaokuan, the naval commander and director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, came to Shanghai yesterday. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency met with Chen at the shipyard and asked him about the recent survey handover and the naval vessel disaster relief. The details of the conversation are recorded below.

Handing over the Surveying: Chen said that in the past, China did not pay much attention to maritime surveying and did not have a formal agency dedicated to surveying. Therefore, all matters were handled by the customs. Even today, to find a nautical chart, ships have to purchase them from foreigners. In recent years, the navy has realized that maritime surveying is crucial for national defense. Therefore, on the one hand, it has set up its own bureau and dispatched warships for surveying. At the same time, the customs marine office still dispatched its Zhuan Tiao and Liuxing surveying cruisers to survey outside the port. Now that the navy has a dedicated bureau, the customs surveying should be transferred for the sake of unifying authority. Moreover, the navy has almost completed surveying the coastline along the Yangtze River and the coast of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian in the past two years. Only a few important port shores have not been surveyed. Therefore, the Ministry of the Navy has repeatedly negotiated with the customs to take over the surveying. Currently, the section from Jiangyin to Wusong is being transferred by Wu Guangzong, the director of the Shanghai Naval Surveying Bureau, together with Hanermen, a Westerner from the Customs Marine Office. The specific method of transfer will be completed in about two to three weeks. As for the Zhuan Tiao and Liuxing surveying cruisers under its jurisdiction, they will remain under the management of the customs for the time being due to the lighthouses and buoys outside the port.

Dispatching Warships for Disaster Relief: Hankou originally had the Chuqian and Rensheng cruisers docked there. Later, due to requests from charitable organizations to send warships to rescue the Hankou flood victims and protect the victims, the Xunning, Chuyou, Desheng, and Weisheng cruisers along the Yangtze River were temporarily transferred. However, most of the flood victims fled to higher ground inland, and the warships could not enter, so they have been unable to provide assistance. They are only providing protection. The rumors that the water level along the Yangtze River is rising and that bandits are emerging are not accurate. If they exist, they are only local bandits robbing and looting on the road. The navy currently has warships stationed along the Yangtze River as far west as Jianli and as far south as Changsha and Xiangtan. The navy suffered no losses during the recent typhoon disaster in the Jinghu area. Only the mud at the bottom of the second dock of the shipyard in Shanghai was loosened, and river water poured in. A few places where the transport factory was built along the river were blown down by the wind, but the losses were not significant.

Naval Maneuvers Not Cancelled: Chen Jiliang, the commander of the First Fleet, is leading the Hai Rong, Hai Chou, and other ten warships in naval maneuvers in Minjiang Sadu. The maneuvers must be completed by mid-September. Therefore, the previous report that the Hai Rong was dispatched to Cuba to participate in the opening ceremony of the Overseas Chinese Revolutionary Memorial Tower is unlikely to be realized.

Zhengji General Company Telephones to Confirm

Guangli Ship is Safe

After reports yesterday that the Zhengji Shipping Company's Guangli ship had struck a reef and sunk near Qingdao, causing passengers to drown, the Zhengji Shanghai office said yesterday that it had received a telegram from the Dalian General Company at 10:00 p.m. on the 26th, sent at 3:20 p.m. that day, stating, "Received your telegram. Guangli is safe in Andong." This indicates that the Guangli ship did not strike a reef. It is currently unknown which ship struck a reef near Qingdao, or it may be just a rumor.

Guangsheng Ship

Rescued Sailors Arrive in Shanghai

Relating the Tragic Fate of the Guang Sheng

The Guang Sheng, a ship belonging to Jardine Matheson & Co., encountered a reef and sank in the waters off Wenzhou during the last typhoon. All of the over one hundred people on board perished. Only three sailors were rescued and returned alive. Two of these rescued sailors arrived in Shanghai yesterday. A reporter made a special visit to inquire, and the circumstances they described are as follows:

The True Picture of the Disaster: The Guang Sheng set sail from

Page 14

Shanghai on the eighth of this month, heading for Shantou and Guangzhou. At 10 PM on the ninth, the ship reached Shandou Island, 180 miles from Fuzhou, and encountered a hurricane. The captain intended to seek shelter by the shore, but the wind was fierce and the waves extremely high. The engine failed, and the ship was spun around by the wind. After one night, at 7 AM on the tenth, the ship struck a hidden reef. The engine room was breached, the engine was destroyed, all the cabins took on water, and the electric lights went out. The ship then began to sink. At that time, the waves were over ten feet high. The Guang Sheng was ultimately sunk into the sea by the huge waves.

All Passengers and Crew Died: The Guang Sheng was fully loaded with cargo. There were about sixty passengers who had boarded in Shanghai, and about fifty crew members and sailors. After the accident, the radio was also ineffective. Everyone could only grab life jackets and allow themselves to sink into the sea. By about 8 AM, the entire ship had sunk into the sea. Not a single crew member or passenger survived; all drowned with the ship. There were also over a hundred horses and sheep on board, which also drowned. Among them, sailor Song Fusheng, stoker Su Guiyuan, and helmsman Li Peifang were swept away by the waves. After drifting for sixty hours, they were rescued by fishing boats on the night of the thirteenth.

Seeking Refuge in Dajin: These three sailors were rescued by fishing boats and taken aboard. They were half-dead. The fishing boats took the three men to Gaole Village and Dajin Village. Song and Su were taken in by the Tianxiang Store in Dajin. The next day, Li Peifang was also brought there. The three stayed in Dajin for seven days, inquiring about the Guang Sheng's entire crew and passengers. They learned that all had drowned. On the nineteenth, they boarded a wooden boat to Fuzhou. In addition to the stoker and sailors, there were twenty foreign employees on the Guang Sheng, none of whom survived. Yesterday, Song and Su arrived in Shanghai on the Wanxiang Wheel. Li Peifang remained in Fujian due to illness and has not yet arrived in Shanghai.

Anti-Japanese Association

Reforming the Internal Organization

The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-the-Overseas-Chinese Committee held its seventh executive committee meeting at 4 PM yesterday. The committee members in attendance were Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Tao Baichuan, Zheng Chengqing, Feng Yixian, Chen Songyuan, Zhang Honghai, Xi Yushu, Li Wenjie, Lu Jingshi, Hou Dachun, Fang Jiaobo, Zhang Yichen, Chen Yafu, Lin Kecong, Tang Junsheng, Chen Peide, Lu Xingzhuang, Liu Shimu, Wang Wenhua, and Wang Zhuping, a total of twenty-two people. Tao Baichuan was publicly elected as chairman, with Feng Yixian and Xue Guangqian as secretaries and recorders. The following important resolutions were passed: (1) Discussing the proposal by the Standing Committee to amend the association's charter, dividing the original Inspection Section into Inspection and Investigation Sections, and dividing the Investigation Section into Investigation and Statistics Sections, requesting a public vote. Resolution: Passed, and the charter was amended. Each section shall have one to two deputy directors. Fang Jiaobo was appointed as the director of the Inspection Section, Zheng Chengqing and Lu Xingzhuang as deputy directors, Hou Dachun as the director of the Investigation Section, Chen Peide as deputy director, Chen Songyuan as the director of the Investigation Section, Hu Fengxiang and Yu Hualong as deputy directors, Lu Jingshi as the director of the Statistics Section, and Wang Wenhua and Liu Shibeng as deputy directors. (2) Discussing Committee Member Yu Qiaqing's resignation from all positions held concurrently. Resolution: Resignation from the position of Director of the Foreign Affairs Section and concurrent position as Standing Committee Member was approved, with sincere efforts to retain him. (3) Discussing the nomination of a successor for the Director of the Foreign Affairs Section. Resolution: Chen Tingrui was nominated to concurrently serve as the Director of the Foreign Affairs Section, with Cheng Zhusun and Li Cishan as deputy directors. (4) Discussing the general rules for the collection and management of the Industrial Fund. Resolution: Amended and passed, the full text is as follows:

General Rules for the Collection and Management of the Industrial Fund (1) In order to thoroughly realize the ultimate goal of resisting goods, an industrial fund should be collected for currently temporarily passable Japanese goods, industrial raw materials, and necessities. (2) The industrial fund collected on certain goods should be designated for the establishment of industrial factories for those goods. (3) The amount of industrial funds to be collected for various goods and detailed methods should be drafted by the design committee of this association in consultation with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and submitted to the Executive Committee for approval and implementation. (4) When the industrial fund collected for various industries reaches a predetermined substantial amount, factories should be established immediately. Subsequent collections should be used to expand the factories as needed, in order to gradually reduce the consumption of Japanese goods year by year until domestic production can supply the demand. (5) The industrial funds paid by various industries will be used as shares in the industrial factories. When the factory organization is complete in the future, it will be handled in accordance with the company law. (6) Before the industrial fund reaches a sufficient amount, it must not be transferred to other uses for any reason, nor can it be returned. (7) The fund management method, in addition to three representatives selected by the industry association, municipal chamber of commerce, and representatives of the city, one person designated by this association should also jointly manage the funds until the establishment of the founding meeting. (8) The industrial fund obtained from the collection should be deposited in a reputable bank designated by the management committee to generate interest. It can only be used after the establishment of the preparatory committee. (9) The method for the industry association and the municipal chamber of commerce to select management committee members is based on convening a joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees, and selecting members by secret ballot. The elected members are not limited to executive and supervisory committee members. However, if the industry association has not established a supervisory committee, it may be elected by the executive committee. (10) The initiators of the industrial factory will be those who have paid one-thousandth or more of the total amount of the fund, or who have paid shares equivalent to one-thousandth or more of the total amount of the fund. (11) The preparatory committee of the industrial factory will be organized by the initiators when the fund has been collected to a predetermined substantial amount. The preparatory committee will convene the founding meeting. (12) The articles of association and business policies of the industrial factory shall be handled by the founding meeting. (13) Current executive committee members of this association, except for those related to the industry, shall absolutely not serve as the initiators of the factory, nor shall they be elected as directors or supervisors of the factory. (14) When collecting the industrial fund, this association will issue a pass for the goods and may charge a handling fee, the method of which will be determined separately. (15) These general rules shall be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee of this Association.

Premier's Stamps to Be Used at a Later Date

Post Office to start on the 10th of Next Month

The Directorate General of Posts had previously decided that, starting from September 1st, the new stamps with the portrait of the Premier (in denominations of 1 cent, 4 cents, 1 dime, and 2 dimes) would be used in all postal areas nationwide. The Directorate also ordered the Shanghai Postal Supply Office to allocate these new stamps, with the intention of gradually distributing them to all postal areas nationwide within the month, for uniform use at that time. According to a responsible person at the Directorate speaking to a Guowen News Agency reporter yesterday, the stamps may not be universally available nationwide by September 1st. The Directorate is considering postponing the implementation for three reasons: (1) The postal areas nationwide are vast, and the allocation of quantities is a complicated procedure. Although active efforts have been made to distribute them, the deadline is too close, and it is practically impossible to ensure that all twenty-three postal areas will have received and distributed the stamps by the end of the month. (2) The Director of the Department, Qian Chunqi, and the Director of the Beijing Printing Bureau, Shen Nengyi, have consulted in Beijing with the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications regarding the printing of six types of martyrs' stamps by the Beijing Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance. It was agreed that 200 million martyrs' stamps would be printed within five years, with the printing price increased by 20% according to the usual price. The Beijing Printing Bureau will actively produce the stamps, and a batch of new martyrs' stamps will be published and used in about a month. The Directorate plans to use the Premier's and martyrs' stamps simultaneously. However, since the stamps currently being printed in Beijing still require time, only the Premier's new stamps can be sent out first. The martyrs' stamps will take another month and a half to be available nationwide. (3) The Directorate is postponing the use of the Premier's new stamps to the anniversary of the founding of the National Government on September 10th. The Directorate will submit this to the Ministry of Communications for approval in the coming days.

Eurasia

Plane Still Flew from Beijing to Shanghai Yesterday

Slightly Bumpy

Safe and Sound

Shanghai has been experiencing strong typhoons recently, and ships have been suspended. The Eurasia Company plane was scheduled to fly south on the 26th (every Wednesday from Beijing to Shanghai). For the safety of passengers, the company's two managers urgently telegraphed the Beijing station on the 25th, instructing them to wait for the typhoon to subside before taking off. Although the wind had not completely subsided yesterday morning, it had subsided slightly, so they telegraphed the order to fly south as scheduled. It arrived safely in Shanghai at 4:10 PM in the afternoon. It is reported that the fuselage shook constantly during the journey, but fortunately the pilot was experienced and was not affected. Therefore, two passengers arrived in Shanghai on that flight. Although they felt slightly bumpy, they were all safe and sound.

Xin Yi Li Ship

Yesterday, Due to Rudder Damage and Rapid Tides, It Mistakenly Collided with a U.S. Warship

Very Minor Damage, to Be Repaired by Yi Li

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Xin Yi Li ship of the Yi Li Shipping Company in Shanghai was test-driving to Wusong yesterday when it collided with the U.S. gunboat USS Asheville, which was docked in the Huangpu River off the Bund on Rue Edward VII. The bow of the U.S. warship was damaged, while the ship was unharmed. The company consulted with the captain of the ship and the company directors on how to handle the situation. As a result, the company will be responsible for the repairs. It was decided to discuss the repair plan again today. The details are as follows:

Brief History of Xin Yi Li: The Xin Yi Li ship of the Yi Li Company was purchased from the Austrian government in November of last year. It was originally an Austrian transport ship with a load capacity of 800 tons. After arriving in Shanghai, it was repaired by the Jiangnan Shipyard and converted into a merchant ship, to be used in the future to sail between Wenzhou, Shantou, and Xiamen. Previously, the ship's water rudder engine was slightly damaged and repaired by Xiechangxiang Machinery Factory. It has now been repaired and is docked at the Dada Wharf in Shiliupu. Reason for the Collision: Yesterday, the Xin Yi Li ship was test-driving to Wusong. At 8:30 AM, it lifted anchor from Dada Wharf. When sailing near the Bund on Rue Edward VII at 9:10 AM, the water rudder engine was damaged and could not turn. In addition, the tide was rapid, and there was no way to avoid it. It came into contact with the U.S. gunboat USS Asheville, which was docked there. The iron plate on the bow of the ship was slightly damaged. Fortunately, the Xin Yi Li ship was unharmed.

Resolution of the Aftermath: The captain and commander of the U.S. warship, Haley (transliteration), invited representatives of the Yi Li Shipping Company to discuss how to handle the situation. The owner of the company, Xu Tingzu, personally went to meet with the captain and commander. Because the personal relationship between the two sides has always been harmonious, and although the incident was accidental, the damage was very minor, so both sides were willing to resolve it peacefully. As a result, because the U.S. warship was docked in the Huangpu River, the Yi Li Company hired workers to repair it. It was decided that both sides would discuss the repair plan again today. The Xin Yi Li ship is still docked at the Dada Wharf, and will sail to Wenzhou after the water rudder engine is completely repaired.

Yan Ganyuan's Collection of Calligraphy and Paintings Published

Yan Ganyuan, the master of the Evening Reflection Studio, is skilled in calligraphy and painting, and his name is known at home and abroad. He is especially respected in the art world for his finger painting. However, many Chinese people regret not having seen Yan's art. It is reported that his son, Chonglou, has selected about forty of his best works and had them printed in collotype. It has now been published as a large volume entitled "Collection of Calligraphy and Paintings from the Evening Reflection Studio." The book contains an equal number of calligraphy and paintings. The calligraphy includes various styles from the Zhou, Qin, Han, Wei, Tang, and Song dynasties, with variations in true, cursive, official, seal, running, and regular scripts. The paintings cover landscapes, figures, flowers, birds, and animals, all of which are complete. In addition to brush paintings, there are also finger paintings, each displaying their own unique qualities. This collection is a magnificent spectacle and can also be used for copying and studying. The collection is distributed by the Civilization Bookstore on Nanjing Road, priced at two yuan, with a special price of 20% off.

Humanistic Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 6 Published

The (Humanistic) Monthly, which is valued by the academic community, has been published on schedule and has reached Volume 2, Issue 5. Issue 6 has recently been completed. The text is more interesting and valuable than before. Among them, Huang Yanpei's "(A Glimpse of the Humanistic Statistics of Various Provinces in the Qing Dynasty)" uses a concise and interesting style to describe the distribution of humanities in various provinces during the Qing Dynasty, allowing the general public to understand the number of top scholars, prime ministers, and governors in each province during the Qing Dynasty. Wang Zao's "(The Complete Story of German Disarmament)" details the process of German disarmament after its defeat in the war. Wen Yu's "(The Problem of International Reparations and War Debts in the Past Twelve Years)" continues from the previous issue and provides a detailed analysis of the causes and consequences of President Hoover's recent proposal to suspend the payment of reparations and war debts, based on facts. In addition, Xi Yin's "(Jing Yushan Telegraphed to Request the Withdrawal of the Order to Establish the Grand Prince)" and Jiangdong Adou's "(Notes from the Gu Hongmei Pavilion)" are rare documents that are related to important modern historical materials, not only recording anecdotes about individuals. Gu Junyi's book review, which introduces "(Anthology of Sanqu Yikan)", details the style and function of the qu, with extensive references. The index of magazine highlights contains a total of one thousand nine hundred and fifty-five entries, making the materials more abundant than before. In addition to the Humanities Editorial Office at No. 1 Nanqianjiatang, West End, 110 Rue Lafayette, Rue Alber, Shanghai, Civilization, Crescent, Dajing, Qixin, Nanxin, Beixin, Taidong, Modern, Xiaoxing, Huatong, Shenzhou Guoguang Society, and Life Weekly Society in this city, as well as the Commercial Press in this and other cities, are all acting as sales agents.

Local News Two

Killed Lover with Sharp Blade

Xu Jinlian's Lack of Virtue

Chen Adong's Extreme Measures

Xu Jinlian, a woman from Jiangbei, residing at No. 114 Mingyuanfang, Huade Road, was stabbed to death with a sharp blade at around 9:45 PM last night. The Yangshupu police station dispatched detectives to investigate and apprehend the murderer, and Chen Adong was arrested on the spot, allegedly the culprit. The deceased was 20 years old and worked at the British American Tobacco factory on Huade Road. She met Chen two years ago, lived together, and started a relationship. The woman's occupation was introduced by Chen. Unexpectedly, the two could not treat each other with sincerity. Xu Jinlian had affairs with another man, secretly making things difficult and unsettling Chen. Therefore, the brutal killing of Xu may have stemmed from this. Xu Jinlian lived with her parents and younger sister. When the tragedy occurred last night, her father was also at home. He suddenly heard a scream coming from the woman's room, rushed to check, and saw Chen Adong fleeing. He immediately called the police to arrest him. Chen is 24 years old, also from Jiangbei, and previously worked in the tobacco silk section of the British American Tobacco factory. He will be sent to court today for questioning. When she died, the deceased was wearing a black shirt and white pants, with her hair styled like a fan. She suffered two knife wounds: one in the waist and thigh, and one in the right arm. An autopsy will be conducted today.

Dong Helang

Killed Wife with Three Knives

Wife's Infidelity Leads to Husband's Deadly Act

Stabbed Eight Times, Blood Everywhere

The following are the details of a tragic case that occurred the day before yesterday at around 9:50 PM at Cunjia Crossing, Huxi, in which a husband and wife had a quarrel, and the husband hid three sharp knives and stabbed his wife eight times, endangering her life.

Family Situation: Dong Helang, 28 years old, a local, residing at No. 5 Cunjia Crossing, previously worked at the Edison Electric Light Bulb Factory. He was very sincere, diligent, and frugal, and worked hard to support his family. He married a woman surnamed Li, who is now only 23 years old, also a local. The wife has a beautiful appearance and a slender figure, and is also fond of romance. Since their marriage three years ago, they both worked at the same factory, and their income was barely enough to make ends meet. Therefore, their relationship was still harmonious. However, the wife was young and liked to be pretty, and seeing her husband's simplicity, she eventually became dissatisfied.

Cause of the Conflict: Since Dong was laid off from the factory last year, he stayed at home. Although his wife was still working at the factory, her monthly income was not enough to support the family. Because Dong had no income, he had to resort to pawn to make up for the deficit. As a result, the accumulated debt was quite large. The wife harbored resentment, and her wild ambition grew. Recently, she suddenly had an affair with someone, treating her husband like a stranger. Now, Dong learned that his wife was having an affair and tried to persuade her, but she did not listen and even insulted and scolded him. The other day, Dong had something to do outside and suddenly saw his wife walking away with a man, shoulder to shoulder. Dong was filled with resentment, both resenting his unemployment and the abandonment of his beloved wife. He immediately returned home with a heavy heart, hid three sharp knives, and conceived the idea of killing his wife.

Scene of the Tragedy: It was not until the bell rang nine times in the afternoon that the wife returned from outside. Dong initially said nothing. Moments later, the wife saw her husband's angry expression and prepared to go to bed. Dong suddenly opened his mouth and questioned his wife about what she had been doing outside. As a result, a war of words broke out, and a quarrel ensued. Dong suddenly jumped up, grabbed her, pulled out a knife, and stabbed her twice in the abdomen. The knife fell to the ground, and he pulled out two more knives from his waist and stabbed her six times in the legs. The wife fell to the ground in extreme pain, bleeding profusely. The landlord of the second room saw the tragic scene and, unable to bear it, immediately called the police, who arrested them both and took them back to the Sixth District Police Station.

Interrogation: After receiving the report, District Chief Ren immediately sent the wife to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment due to her severe injuries. According to the doctors, the injuries were very serious and her life was in danger. According to Dong Helang's statement, his wife, Li, had been having an affair with someone recently, and he had tried to persuade her, but she had insulted and scolded him, so he was filled with resentment and committed this heinous act. District Chief Ren, considering the case involved wielding a knife to injure someone, prepared a document yesterday to send the case to the local court for questioning.

Dafeng Silk Shop Accused

Selling Counterfeit Fuchou Silk

Counterfeiting the Single and Double Deer Brand Fuchou Silk

Also Using Other People's Names

Luo and Pang File a Lawsuit

Losses Sought are Divided into Two Parts

Shen Zicha, shareholder and manager of Dafeng Silk Shop on Hankou Road, and Jin Liquan, a shareholder of the shop, are being sued by Luo Kunxiang and Pang Zhuqing, the owners of Jiucheng Qiaji and Waicheng Zhiji silk shops, respectively, for counterfeiting their Single and Double Deer brand fuchou silk trademarks and falsely using their names. Luo and Pang have hired lawyers to file a criminal self-suit in the First Special District Local Court, requesting that they be punished according to law, and have also filed a private suit, demanding compensation for losses of silver 19,362 taels, in a major case of trademark forgery. The case is quite complex, and the court has held several hearings, but it has not yet concluded. The following is a summary of the content:

Luo and Pang Each Establish a Shop: Luo and Pang had previously partnered to open Jiucheng Fuchou Silk Shop, and used Single Deer and Double Deer as their trademarks. They successively registered patents with the Beijing Government and the National Government. Shen Zicha was originally an employee of Jiucheng, but later Luo and Pang split up and each ran a shop, both using the name Jiucheng, but Luo added Qiaji and Pang added Zhiji.

Shen Establishes Dafeng Silk Shop: After Luo and Pang split up, Shen joined Jin Liquan and others to establish Dafeng Silk Shop. He knew that Jiucheng's fuchou silk was selling very well and making excellent profits, so he counterfeited the trademarked goods and secretly sold them. Luo and others had heard about it for some time, but they had no evidence and did not negotiate with him.

Double Deer Fuchou Silk Discovered: On June 25th of this year, Luo Kunyang, a partner of Jiucheng Qiaji, delivered goods to the warehouse of French merchant Bo Xing Foreign Firm in the French Concession. He suddenly saw a large amount of Single and Double Deer brand fuchou silk stacked there, and the trademarks were all counterfeit. According to the manager of the foreign firm, Qi Qian, and the street vendor, Qiu Liansheng, they were sold by Dafeng.

Prices Lower Than Jiucheng's: Luo Kunyang reported this to the French Consul and requested that a search warrant be issued, ordering the French police to rush to the Bo Xing warehouse and seize 900 pieces of early-brand fuchou silk and store them in the French Consulate. He also went to Bo Xing Foreign Firm to investigate the account books and learned that since December of last year, more than 29,561 pieces of the brand fuchou silk had been shipped out, of which 21,010 pieces were marked as purchased from Dafeng. The prices were all lower than Jiucheng's.

Counterfeiting Names and Trademarks: Luo then reported this to the Public Concession police, who requested the First Special District Court to issue a warrant and send police to search Dafeng Silk Shop. They seized ten relevant account books and calculated that since last year, the total number of fuchou silk sold to Bo Xing was 25,764 pieces, of which 11,361 pieces were marked with Single Deer and Double Deer trademarks. The number of counterfeit goods of the brand was 34,134 pieces. In addition to counterfeiting the trademark, the advertisements were also counterfeiting the names of Jiu Zhiji and Pang Zhuqing. Therefore, they began to negotiate with Shen et al.

Two Parts of the Lawsuit: Shen claimed that the goods were purchased from Pang Chunsheng, a street vendor for Jiucheng Zhiji, and that he was reselling them to Bo Xing. He also said that Chunsheng was Pang Zhuqing's nephew. However, Pang Zhuqing absolutely denied having such a nephew, believing that Shen Jin was making excuses to evade responsibility. Therefore, they requested that he be punished according to law. As for the losses sought, they are divided into two parts: (1) The forged goods sold by the defendant amount to at least 34,134 pieces. Calculating the profit per piece at 2 taels, the compensation should be 68,268 taels. (2) Since the discovery of the counterfeit goods, the sales of Luo and Pang's shops have declined sharply. The loss suffered by each family is 100,000 taels. Therefore, at a minimum, compensation of 100,000 taels should be ordered. However, the defendant has also hired a lawyer to defend himself. The trial has concluded and a verdict is scheduled for next Monday.

After Lin Yunfang Fled

Seized His Deposited Luggage

Wooden Boxes Full of Antiques

Leather Suitcases Full of Clothes

Lin Yunfang, the director of the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy and a native of Guangdong, embezzled more than 110,000 yuan of public funds and fled secretly on August 4th. The shipyard reported the case and issued a wanted notice, but he has not been found yet. Zhang Zhiqin, the chief detective of the General Patrol Room, and Mei Sheng, the Western detective, discovered that Lin had two wooden boxes and six leather suitcases deposited with his friend Gao Dagang at No. 370 Haig Road. They requested the First Special District Court to issue a search warrant and seized the eight boxes from Gao's house the other day. Upon opening them, the wooden boxes were full of antiques and the leather suitcases were full of clothes, estimated to be worth about 5,000 to 6,000 yuan. Yesterday morning, the patrol room lawyer, Ru Baoyi, requested the court to dispose of them. Judge Xu Jiashi ordered that the seized clothes be detained for future compensation.

Shen Chengfu's Home

Guns and Hunting Rifles Seized

All Disposed of Separately by the Court

Shen Chengfu, a comprador of the British merchant Taihe Foreign Firm at No. 15 Bowuyuan Road, a native of Shaoxing, recently embezzled several million yuan of public funds and fled secretly. The firm reported the case to the police and requested the First Special District Court to issue a warrant for his arrest. The patrol room seized three of Shen's cars and requested the court to impound them, as reported in this newspaper. The other day, Geng Debiao, the Chinese detective of the General Patrol Room, and Huai Aituo, the Western detective, were ordered to search Shen's residence at No. 2, 1168F Jingansi Lane, Jingan Temple Road. They seized five pistols and 535 bullets, and two hunting rifles. They reported back to the patrol head, and yesterday morning, lawyer Ru Baoyi, representing the patrol room, applied to the First Criminal Court of the Special Court for disposal. According to lawyer Ru, the serial numbers of the five pistols seized were 609098, 3925, 68, 32475, and 2445. Among them, only 609098 had a license, and the rest were unlicensed. One of the two hunting rifles was deposited by Shen's colleague, a Westerner named Shelang Sikesiji. Therefore, they requested the court to decide how to dispose of them. Subsequently, Western detective Huai Aituo reported the search situation. Criminal Judge Xu Jiashi reviewed the report and ordered that one hunting rifle be returned to Shelang Sikesiji, and the licensed pistol and hunting rifle and documents should be detained. The unlicensed pistols and bullets should be confiscated and first handed over to the patrol room for inspection.

Shangsong Road to Open Soon

It Has Been Decided that the Beiwai Line Will Be Trial-Run Starting September 10th

The section of the Shangsong County Road from Beiqiao Station on the Shanghai-Min Road west to Weiqiao, about twelve li, is under the construction of Shanghai County. The construction of this item was completed early. From Weiqiao to the West Gate of Songjiang, about eighteen li, is under the construction of the Songjiang County Construction Bureau. They are now building bridges and paving roads, working hard. The Weiqiao, which is the border between Shangsong and Songjiang Counties, has been approved by the Construction Department to be jointly managed and will soon be started and built. The Shangsong Company, which contracted the road line, was organized and established early, and vehicles have been prepared for a long time. The stations along the way have been completed one after another. It was originally planned to run the entire road on August 1st, but due to the three-in-one earthworks and the Weiqiao project, it was slightly delayed. Yesterday, it was learned that the company's manager, Yin Shisheng, in order to consolidate the roadbed, which had been built with weeds, decided to first conduct a trial run of the Beiwai long-distance bus in early September to facilitate local transportation. Once the Weiqiao, jointly built by the two counties, is completed, the entire road will be open to traffic. It is said that the route is connected to the Songsijiao Road, and in the future, it will be able to reach Sheshan directly.

The Meaning of the Dongjiang Identity Case

In the case of lawyer Dong Yu and his wife Jiang's appeal for confirmation of identity, it was heard in the Jiangsu High Court on the 15th of this month. Because the witnesses were not complete, it was necessary to summon and examine them again. Zhang Yaozeng, the lawyer hired by Jiang, specially submitted a written argument. The following is a transcript:

Regarding the submission of a supplementary written argument, the appellant and Dong Yu's case for confirmation of identity and request for alimony has been debated by the court on the 15th of this month. The appellee, Dong Yu, stated that the Shanghai French Concession Court's judgment on July 8th approved the divorce of the two parties. According to Article 5 of the Annex to the Sino-French New Agreement, this matter has been determined, and the appellant has lost the qualification of the party. His agent also made the same statement in court and submitted a photo of the judgment of the French Concession Court as evidence. After the appellant filed a detailed rebuttal of the facts and the law, the matter is of great importance, and I am deeply afraid that the records at the time may not be detailed. I hereby submit the written arguments as follows: Part 1 Regarding the facts, in November of last year, the appellee, Dong Yu, filed a lawsuit in the Shanghai French Concession Court for divorce on the grounds that the appellant had lung disease. After several trials, in February of this year, the plaintiff, namely the appellee, suddenly applied to declare an indefinite postponement. The appellant wandered without a home and had no choice but to file a lawsuit in the Special District Local Court for confirmation of identity and separate maintenance. The court then lawfully transferred the case to the Shanghai Local Court for trial and judgment. The appellant refused to accept the judgment and appealed to the court in accordance with the law, and was waiting for the hearing. Suddenly, the French Concession Court reheard the original case, which had been suspended for a long time. The appellant immediately filed a statement, stating that the previous trial was only due to consideration of the treaty, but now that it belongs to the Jiangsu High Court, we respect Chinese law and it is difficult to respond to the trial. Repeated summonses were not answered. When the court opened the trial on July 21, the appellee did not attend for reasons and declared the debate closed. Then, he requested to reopen the debate. At the end of July, the Sino-French New Agreement was announced, and the appellee suddenly declared that the French Concession Court had already made a judgment and that it was now determined to be valid, and that the Jiangsu High Court would be unable to revive the case. The appellant was deeply shocked and inquired everywhere. The member of the court confirmed that all cases were judged uniformly at the end, so this case is known to be so, but since it was not served, nor was the time of the pronouncement of the judgment clearly indicated, on August 8, he submitted a presentation to the Third High Branch Court of Jiangsu, requesting service and declaring that he would reserve the appeal. This is the actual situation of the case. Among them, there are extremely noteworthy ones: (1) After the case was appealed to this court, the French Concession Court suddenly reheard the case, which had been declared suspended, obviously intending to resist the legal proceedings. (2) After reading the appellant's statement, the French Concession Court knew that the case was legally under the jurisdiction of the second-instance legal system, but still brazenly proceeded with the judgment, obviously disregarding Chinese legal rights. (3) The appellee's reply submitted after July 21 did not mention the judgment of the French Concession Court at all, so it is questionable whether the judgment was made on July 8. (4) Since the judgment of the French Concession Court has not been served, how could the appellee be able to obtain the full text of it alone, and be able to take a photo of the original? Part 2 Regarding the legal part, the appellee, relying on Article 5 of the Annex to the Sino-French Agreement on the Establishment of Chinese Courts in the Shanghai French Concession, argued that the divorce judgment of the French Concession Court has been determined and that this case cannot be established, which is a misunderstanding. The legal interpretation of Article 5 of the Annex refers specifically to cases in dispute in the French Concession Court. Those cases that are simultaneously in Chinese courts outside the French Concession and are proceeding legally are not included. There are three reasons for this: Article 5 of the Annex does not mean that all judgments of the French Concession Court have a determined effect, but limits those that are in dispute or have been suspended for a long time and are not subject to change. This is to maintain the stability of the legal relationship. The intent of this article, which excludes cases that have already been sued or can still be appealed, is very clear. Therefore, if the same legal relationship is in dispute in the French Concession Court and is also legally proceeding in the Chinese court, even if one side's French Concession Court has made a judgment, the other side's Chinese court proceedings are still in progress and have not been interrupted. The dispute relationship has not ended, there is no so-called reversal, and there is no reason to prohibit its progress. Therefore, it is naturally not subject to the application of this article, this is one. Article 5 of the Annex gives legal effect to the previous illegal judgments of the French Concession Court, and the intention is only this. There is absolutely no reason to overturn the previous legal procedures of the Chinese courts. Therefore, its application is naturally limited to cases that are tried in the French Concession Court and have not been involved in Chinese courts. If cases that are simultaneously involved in Chinese courts are also subject to application, this is to overturn the previous legal procedures, which is not the original intention of the legislation, this is two. According to the precedents of the former Dali Court and the customary laws of various courts, the judgments of the French Concession Court are invalid. All judgments of the French Concession Court are still accepted and judged when lawsuits are later filed in Chinese courts, so as to distinguish between legality and illegality and guide the people to follow. If Article 5 of the Annex is interpreted broadly, saying that cases that are simultaneously involved in the French Concession Court and the Chinese Court are also subject to application, then those who violated the law and acted arbitrarily in the past will be protected, and those who obeyed the law and sought justice will be ruined. How will the prestige of the national law be compared before and after, this is three. According to this case and the subject matter of the lawsuit requested by the appellee in the French Concession Court are different, but the facts and legal relationship in dispute are completely the same, and it is a case that is simultaneously involved in the French Concession Court and the Chinese Court. According to the above explanation, the progress of this case cannot be prevented due to the judgment of the French Concession Court. Furthermore, there is a big question as to whether the judicial organs can immediately invoke Article 5 of the Annex. In the past, although cases were judged by the French Concession Court, the parties could still freely file lawsuits in Chinese courts. Now, as a result of the provisions of Article 5, all those who could still file lawsuits in the courts in the past cannot file lawsuits because the judgment is valid. This is clearly a regulation restricting the people's right to sue. According to Article 21 of the Covenant, the people have the right to sue in the courts according to the law. If you want to restrict this right to sue, you must do so according to the law. Article 5 of the Annex is not the law. Some say that the treaty has the same effect as the law, and the annex to the agreement is a treaty, and it is not impossible to replace the law. However, the treaty has a certain form in international law. Regardless of whether the annex is clearly an exchange of notes and does not conform to the treaty form, even if its substance is a kind of treaty, according to Article 29 of the National Government Organization Law, the treaty case must be resolved by the Legislative Yuan. Now the annex has not yet been resolved by the Legislative Yuan, so it is known that it has not yet become a treaty. To use an exchange of notes that has not yet become a treaty to restrict the people's right to sue, which cannot be restricted without the law, is a violation of the Covenant. The judicial organs have the duty to maintain the law, and there is no obligation to invoke the rules that obviously violate the law. The above two items are stated according to the facts, and I beg the court to carefully investigate and make a fair judgment, which is for the benefit of morality. Respectfully presented to the Jiangsu High Court, the person presenting the case is Jiang Shi, agent lawyers Zhang Yaozeng, Yuan Jingtang, Sheng Shenghiu.

Fire Department and Emergency Automobile Department

Have Switched to Automatic Telephone

Shanghai Municipal Council Notice of Communication Method

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession announced that the telephone numbers of the Fire Department and the Emergency Automobile Department have been changed to the automatic telephone number 15440. For non-automatic telephones, you can call to connect. After connecting, you must indicate whether it is a fire alarm or an accident. Speak slowly and clearly, report the street name, house number, and the nearest intersection or cross street, and report the telephone number used so that the person answering the call can understand clearly. After the call has been answered, a person should be sent to the road to wait for the fire truck or emergency automobile to guide them, so as not to delay.

Remaining News After the Big Storm

The Eye of the Storm Fortunately Changed Direction

The Water Level of the Huangpu River Broke Records

The Shanghai Times reported that the fierceness of this typhoon was the greatest of all the typhoons this summer. According to meteorological reports, between 9:00 and 10:00 PM on Tuesday night, its eye was originally heading directly for this port, but it suddenly encountered high pressure in the northwest and turned to the northeast, blowing through the mouth of the Yangtze River and Chongming, fifty or sixty miles from Shanghai. At that time, the wind speed reached 100 miles per hour. If it had not changed direction temporarily, its eye would have blown through Shanghai, and the loss of life and property would have been incalculable.

The North-China Daily News reported that the water level of the Huangpu River on Tuesday night broke the highest record of 1921. According to the water gauge in the Bund Park, the water level of the Huangpu River on August 20 of that year was 14.3 feet higher than the lowest water line. This time it was 14.8 feet higher than the lowest water line. The total amount of loss this time is still unestimated, but it is expected not to be too large, and the damage caused by street flooding will be the main one. It is also said that 300 trees were blown down on the Shanghai Municipal Council's property inside and outside the concession, and the situation in the French Concession was roughly the same.

Two People Died from Electrocution One After Another

Worker and Rickshaw Puller

In the front days on Lujiazhai Road, Zhabei, a power line was blown down by the wind and fell on the ground. A man who looked like a worker in his thirties passed by and was electrocuted to the ground. At that time, a rickshaw puller Wu Linju passed by and saw the man fall on the ground. He did not know that he was electrocuted, so he pulled him with his hand, which caused the electricity to pass through his body, and he was also paralyzed to death by the electric current. The Five District Police Station ordered the local guarantor Yan Liugen to report the case to the local court for autopsy. Prosecutor Wang and others arrived at the scene and separately verified and clarified that they should be collected and buried.

Rickshaw Puller Hangs Himself on a Tree

The Deceased's Wife Claims He Was Driven to It by a Police Officer's Debt Collection

Yao Xiangzhou, a 26-year-old from Funing, resided in Hengkang Lane, Guangzhou Road, Zhabei, and worked as a rickshaw puller. Yesterday, at 12:20 PM, in front of No. 23 Wangjia Sha, he used his own belt to hang himself from a tree. After being discovered, a report was made to the Xinzha Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. They found Yao hanging from the tree, about three to four feet off the ground, with rickshaw No. 3240 parked below. He was taken down, but was already dead. The body was transported to the Philand Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, a prosecutor from the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Wei Ligong and clerk Liu Chun, arrived to examine the body. Yao Zhou, the deceased's wife, testified, stating that her husband had borrowed five yuan from Chinese police officer No. 1481 in April, and had been gradually paying it back, but still owed over twenty cents. In the past few days, her husband had been unable to pull a rickshaw due to illness. The night before, her husband went out to pull the rickshaw, but the officer insisted on him returning the debt. Her husband had no money, so the officer took away his license, which she believed led to his suicide. However, she did not know about the hanging at the time. Prosecutor Guo then declared that Yao Xiangzhou had indeed died by hanging himself. The body was released to his wife, Yao Zhou, for burial.

Husband and Wife Quarrel, Wife Hangs Herself

Wang Bu Xing, the second son of Wang Kaitian, a native of Taizhou, resided at No. 18 Chenjia Zhai, Miaotou, South Railway Station. He was married to Wang Yang, 24 years old. The affection between husband and wife was not strong, and they often quarreled. The other day, they argued again over a trivial matter. The woman felt deeply resentful, returned to her room, and wept. Shortly after, she hanged herself. By the time she was discovered and attempts were made to save her, it was too late. Yesterday, the First Section of the First District summoned Wang and others for questioning, and ordered the head of the twelfth tu to report to the local court for an examination. Prosecutor Yang and others arrived at the scene and confirmed that it was a suicide by hanging. They ordered the family to collect the body for burial pending further investigation.

Xu Yueqin Commits Suicide by Smoking Opium

Xu Yueqin, a Guangdong woman, 18 years old, lived with her brother Xu Shijiu and others at No. 2 Baochang Road, Zhabei. Recently, she had been betrothed to someone, but Yueqin, being of a romantic nature, still went out to play frequently. Her brother Xu Shijiu repeatedly advised her against it. The other day, because Yueqin returned late at night, Shijiu scolded her. Yueqin, in a moment of anger, secretly consumed opium in order to commit suicide. Her brother noticed and immediately rushed her to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but because she had taken the poison for too long, the treatment was ineffective and she soon died. The hospital notified the Hongkou Police Station, which dispatched detectives to send the body to the Philand Road morgue. A report was filed with the First Special District Court, which sent Prosecutor Guo and others to the morgue to confirm that the death was due to poisoning. They ordered her brother, Xu Shijiu, to collect the body for burial pending review.

Only Recognizes Her Brother, Not Her Husband

The Personal Dispute Between Zhao Yu and Zhao Jianzhuo

Zhao Yu, 22-year-old wife of Zhao Jianfu from Fuyang, secretly fled to Shanghai at the end of the fourth lunar month last year and hid at No. 19 Wanzhu Road. Recently, Zhao's nephew, Shichang, sent a letter to his uncle, who came to Shanghai yesterday and took Yu to the First Section of the Second District to be investigated and to request that Yu be ordered to return home with her husband. According to Zhao Yu, "I have been Zhao Jianfu's adopted daughter since I was a child. Zhao Jianfu is my brother, not my husband, so I do not want to return home with Jianfu." As the case involved a marital dispute, Zhao was instructed to file a lawsuit in court himself.

Robbery of a Rice Boat

Searching for Silver: Beating People: Cargo

Ji Weixiang, a rice merchant, recently sold rice he had brought from Songjiang in Shanghai, earning over two thousand yuan. He planned to return and used the money to buy 500 bags of flour. He had more than 600 yuan left, which he divided into two packages and hid under the stove before setting sail. The other day, while sailing in Desheng, a hurricane suddenly broke out, so he anchored at the edge of the river to shelter from the wind. Unexpectedly, the next morning, a pirate ship arrived with seven or eight bandits, who swarmed onto the boat. They asked the watchmen what was going on and then tied them up, gagging them with cloth. The bandits got off the ship. Ji woke up from his sleep, shouting and was threatened by the bandits who pulled out guns, preventing him from making noise. They forced Ji to hand over the silver, but he refused. He was beaten and injured. Ji, in unbearable pain, had to reveal where the silver was hidden. After the bandits searched under the stove and found the silver, they beat Ji again, considering him extremely cunning, forcing him to reveal if there was silver elsewhere. Ji said there was no silver anywhere else. The bandits searched Ji's body and took away another sixty or seventy yuan and a watch. Before leaving, they also took more than twenty bags of flour, loaded them onto the pirate ship, and sailed south in a hurry. After the bandits left, some of the crew untied the watchmen. Ji sailed the boat back to Minhang and sent the injured crew to the hospital for treatment. It is said that the crew were seriously injured and unable to speak, and Ji also suffered internal injuries and was vomiting blood.

Stealing Hometown Salted Meat to Gamble

Sentenced to Two Months in Prison

Shen A'si, from Jiangbei, stole thirty-eight pieces of hometown salted meat and six hams from Chen Guiquan's restaurant at No. 15 Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession. He sold them to Wang A'san at No. 312 Hubei Road, Cao Shuzhen at No. 682 Minguo Road, and the Deshen Pavilion on Tianzhutang Street, earning a total of ninety yuan, which he used for gambling. After the owner reported it to the police station, Detective Bao discovered and arrested Shen, along with the stolen hams. Yesterday, he was sent to the Summary Court of the Second Special District for questioning. First, the police lawyer explained the case, and the owner complained about the theft. When questioned, Shen admitted that he stole the salted meat due to poverty. He said that all the money he got had been gambled away. Judge Wu Fanglian verified the confession and immediately sentenced the defendant to two months of imprisonment. The number of days detained before the verdict will be counted as two days to offset one day of imprisonment.

Zhang Desen, a native of Fengtian, who worked as a Chinese servant for a Westerner at No. 50 Shanzhong Road in the French Concession, was hired in Fengtian. Because he was trusted and favored by his master, he came to Shanghai. However, Zhang was addicted to opium and liked to gamble. He has now reported to the police station to investigate. If anyone knows the whereabouts of Zhang, please report to the French Police Station or his employer's house.

Abduction Case Aboard the Lushan Maru

Xu Cuizhen, Young and Deceived

Pan Afu, Deserves to Die

Xu Cuizhen, a young woman from Hangzhou, 18 years old, married Lao Xu, who lived near the train station, last year. Because her family was poor and could not make a living, she came to Shanghai to work as a helper, living at her uncle's house in Xujiahui. Not even three days had passed. The other day, while going out to buy cigarettes, she was met by the kidnapper Pan Afu (50 years old, from Wenzhou), who used his means of seducing women to lure Xu Cuizhen to a inn and had intercourse with her for one night, feigning affection and vowing to be husband and wife, boasting of his wealthy family in Wenzhou, so she would not have to suffer back in Hangzhou. Cuizhen, deceived by him, deeply believed him. Pan then colluded with Chen Axi to take Cuizhen aboard the Lushan Maru steamer to Xiamen for sale, telling the woman that they were returning to his home in Wenzhou to live as husband and wife forever. If anyone questioned them, they would say they were husband and wife. However, before the ship set sail, investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang from the Relief Society, along with police detective Deng Jiagen from the Water Police Station, boarded the ship and questioned Cuizhen. She only said she was going to Wenzhou, and the rest of her answers were inconsistent. The investigators knew that she was being abducted, and that Pan was 50 years old and Xu was 18 years old, which was an unlikely match. The language spoken in Wenzhou and Hangzhou was different, and Axi was not a relative. They were all taken to the Water Police Station and questioned. The truth immediately came out. Yesterday, they were transferred to the local court for questioning.

Dalai Steamer Uncovers Smuggling of Opium

The American Dalai Company's overseas class [blank] steamer, after arriving in Shanghai, was docked between buoys No. 11 and 12 near Bailianjing on the South Huangpu River. Zheng Liansheng, the stoker foreman of the steamer, and Chuan Zhongyu, the hold supervisor, secretly purchased 250 cans of opium paste, each can weighing 50.5 taels, totaling 1,375 taels, and hid it in the stoker's hold, intending to smuggle it abroad for sale. At 6:10 PM the other night, Ge Changsheng, a detective from the Customs Water Police Station, boarded the ship and discovered it, arresting Zheng and Fu together. They were taken to the police station. Zheng, 40 years old, from Ningbo, and Fu, 22 years old, from Ningbo, both confessed to smuggling opium paste for profit. The police chief ordered all the opium paste to be handed over to the customs for burning, and the two criminals will be sent to the local court for questioning.

The pre-order period ends on September 15, and the book will be published on October 15, distributed by Shanghai Trust Company.

The general tourists who saw them all praised the swimsuits for their fine quality, beautiful colors, and indistinguishability from imported goods.

Sixth District Council Member Loses Identification Papers, Now Void

Educational News

Special Feature

What is the Effectiveness of Supplementary Education?

Jiang Wenyu (1)

Generally speaking, supplementary education is primarily designed for young people who have graduated from primary school, are unable to continue their education due to financial constraints, and are currently engaged in agricultural, industrial, or commercial occupations. The purpose is to use their spare time after work to supplement them with the necessary knowledge and skills for their occupations, as well as scientific common sense related to their occupations. At the same time, considerable guidance is also given to the moral and service ethics of citizens who are working to make a living. Because the targets of this type of education are young people serving in the workforce, and the supplementary curriculum focuses on the inculcation and training of occupational knowledge and skills, it is often classified within the scope of vocational education in the educational system, or simply referred to as (vocational supplementary education).

If we briefly examine the history of supplementary education in modern civilized countries, the initial facilities were generally as described above. However, things have gradually changed in recent years. Because the educational trend is towards popularization, the educational system is also moving towards socialization. Therefore, from a horizontal perspective, everyone should be able to receive higher education. From a vertical perspective, it is natural to gradually improve the level of this informal supplementary education, and we absolutely do not want the right to education to be monopolized by a small number of people. Without discussing European and American countries, let's take Japan as an example. In recent years, the (subject system) of supplementary education has gradually evolved into the (academic year system). In the past, supplementary education mostly aimed to specialize in one or two subjects. Once a subject was completed, the education was considered finished. And so-called certain subjects were mostly limited to occupations, but recently, they are no longer entirely limited to subjects. Many have been changed to (academic year,) which means that in addition to specializing in occupational subjects, they also pay attention to other cultural education subjects, in order to provide students with complete training, so that they can both make a living and be good people. Therefore, the focus is now on academic years rather than (subjects). Not only that, but as with the youth training center approach, in addition to occupational training and personal cultivation, more attention is paid to military training, which is especially a special type of supplementary education. When it comes to the curriculum, it is divided into several levels, the lowest equivalent to the early stages of middle school, and the highest exceeding middle school and approaching the initial stages of specialized subjects. When we see the situation in one place in Japan, it is not difficult to infer the situation in other countries. Originally, (nothing is difficult in the world, as long as you have the will.) Despite growing up in a poor family, being unable to continue schooling after primary school graduation, and immediately becoming an apprentice in a shop or factory, being able to study for two or three hours every day after work, continuously for eight or ten years, their level may not be inferior to that of a high school graduate, and may not be inferior to the first or second year of a specialized school. I think, as long as there is an institution that provides this kind of education, there will definitely be this kind of hardworking and outstanding youth. Isn't this already a trend in Japan now? Furthermore, university lectures and night universities can also be included in the scope of supplementary education. Didn't a worker who graduated from primary school in England, because he received supplementary education and went to university lectures, listen for many years, and become a minister in a certain department once the cabinet was reorganized? Everyone, please don't look down on this (unorthodox) unofficial education. You must know that there are quite a few talented and capable people who did not come from formal channels.

Speaking of our China, formal school education has not yet been popularized, and has not yet been done properly. It has even caused many bad phenomena in society because of the existence of schools, causing the general public to be heartbroken. How can we even talk about informal school education or supplementary education? However, my opinion is not like this. I believe that because formal school education has not been popularized, because formal school education has not been done well, and because society is dissatisfied with the current schools, supplementary education should be given special attention, using it to make up for the shortcomings and solve various difficulties. Therefore, in recent years, I have often discussed with friends the current educational problems in China. Everyone sighs and believes that all kinds of problems have arisen. Finally, I strongly advocate for supplementary education, saying that in today's China, it has the effect of curing (educational illnesses) and is worth promoting by everyone. I remember that I had a nearly arbitrary statement:

Important News

Jiangsu Province

All Counties Pay Attention to Teacher In-Service Training

The education bureaus of various counties in Jiangsu Province, in order to promote the popularization of education, should pay close attention to teacher training, in order to expand the quantity and ensure the quality. Since 1929, the various counties in Jiangsu have been preparing for the Joint Office for Compulsory Education, and have established correspondence departments for teacher training. On the one hand, unqualified teachers are engaged in in-service training and tutoring, making it easier to participate in certification exams (and those with excellent results can also serve as primary school principals or teachers). It has been found that there are 11,673 unqualified teachers in the teacher registration of various counties, exceeding half of the teacher quota. On the other hand, qualified teachers can instill new knowledge and improve their educational efficiency through the interaction of teaching and learning. This training graduates in one year, which is quite cost-effective and yields great benefits. The Ministry of Education has specially praised it, and the education departments of Zhejiang and Fujian provinces have also followed suit. The department is now recruiting the third batch of students. All the lecture notes on teaching methods are checked against the new curriculum standards recently established by the Ministry of Education and re-edited. Therefore, most of the members of the curriculum standards committee are also editors and instructors of the department, so they can connect with each other. Each course of lecture notes is attached with detailed homework guidance and reference materials, using methods such as questions and answers, tests, surveys, visits, and practical exercises to conduct thorough research. All participating students should register with the education bureau, and each county has also established subsidy and incentive research methods, assigning teachers to participate according to the school district. The registration period for students from other provinces and counties is extended to the end of September.

Jiangsu Provincial Authorities Emphasize Fisheries Education

Starting with Training Talents

China's fishing industry adheres to outdated methods and does not know how to improve, causing the East adjacent countries to constantly invade coastal areas, causing frequent disputes. Recently, the Department of Agriculture and Mines of Jiangsu Province, in view of this, has specifically formulated the Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Guidance Personnel Training Measures, and has recruited two fisheries trainees at the Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Experiment Site in Xiaobeimen, Shanghai, specifying that they are limited to those with Chongming and Guanyun county registration, because the fishing profits of the two counties are very large and are often seized by the Japanese. If we do not remedy it quickly, we will be unable to recover. The fisheries guidance stations attached to the agricultural improvement sites in Nantong, Rugao, Yancheng, and Changshu counties also recruit two people in each county for training. High school graduates with aspirations can send letters to the Shanghai Fisheries Experiment Site or the county sites to request detailed regulations. It is heard that the training method is set for two to three years, stipulating that there are two months of lessons each year, totaling 288 hours, and two months of assisting work and eight months of practice. The Jiangsu Provincial Education Bureau also established a fisheries village normal school at the old site of the Guanyun Xugou Fisheries Training Institute (the starting point of the eastern section of the Longhai Railway) this year, because the fishing villages are vast and there is no education to speak of. The qualifications for admission are the same as for ordinary rural teachers, and the entrance examination will be held on September 1 and 2 at the Haizhou Donghai Middle School headquarters.

Statistics on Students Going to Europe and the United States

Total of Over Eighty People

Thirteen Female Students

Fewer than in Previous Years

According to the Global Chinese Students Association, the number of students going to Europe and the United States this summer is estimated to be over eighty, with about forty going to Europe and about forty going to the United States. Among those going to Europe, the number going to France is the largest, followed by Belgium, then Germany, and the fewest to the United Kingdom. (1) Among those going to France, the most are in law, followed by political science. There are also several in fine arts, physics, chemistry, economics, philosophy, and biology. (2) Among those going to Belgium, the most are in law and political science, followed by engineering, and the fewest in liberal arts. (3) Among those going to Germany, the most are in medicine, followed by political economy, and the fewest in engineering. (4) Among those going to the United Kingdom, the most are in political economy, followed by education and engineering, and the fewest in literature. (5) Among those going to the United States, the most are in business, followed by engineering, then journalism and medicine. There are very few in agriculture, physics, chemistry, literature, law, and politics. There are thirteen female students in this session, eight of whom are going to the United States and five to Europe. Some of those going to Europe have already set sail on the French mail ship Anter Lai朋 on August 1 and the Japanese mail ship Fushimi丸 on August 18. Some will depart on the French mail ship Maxin General on August 29. Some of those going to the United States have also already set sail on the British mail ship Canadian Queen on August 18 and the American mail ship Lincoln and the Japanese mail ship Taiyo丸 on August 21. Some will depart on the British mail ship Russian Queen on August 31.

He Bingsong, etc.

Periodic Memorial for Chen Hangshu

At the Chinese Science Society at 1 PM on the 30th

Mr. Chen Hangshu, former secretary and lecturer of Guanghua University, went to France in the 16th year of the Republic of China (1927) to specialize in economics at the University of Paris. He suddenly contracted peritonitis and passed away in the hospital on May 3rd of this year. His friends He Bingsong, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Songgao, He Zhongchi, Ma Chonggan, and others have arranged a memorial service to be held at 2 PM on the afternoon of the 30th of this month (Sunday) at the Mingfu Library Hall of the Chinese Science Society on Albert Road, Avenue See Ahms, in the French Concession of this city. A brief biography of Mr. Chen is recorded below:

Mr. Chen, given name Xunshu, courtesy name Hangshu, surname Chen, was from Zixi, Zhejiang. He was exceptionally intelligent from a young age. At the age of thirteen, he graduated from a village school and entered Xiaoshi Middle School in the county seat. In the tenth year of the Republic of China (1921), he entered St. John's University in Shanghai to study economics and political science. In the summer of the fourteenth year of the Republic of China (1925), the May Thirtieth Incident occurred, and the British president of St. John's University, Bu Fangji, prohibited students from participating in the movement. The entire faculty and students left the school in anger and organized a post-departure committee. Mr. Chen devoted himself to writing and publicity. Later, in the establishment of Guanghua University, Mr. Chen's efforts in planning and organization were considerable. After the new school was completed, he served as secretary to the president and taught political science, comparative political science, and other courses. In November of that year, he married Ms. Hong Shulang. The following year, he went to France to study economics at the University of Paris, also studying social history and other subjects. The Academia Sinica heard of his reputation and invited him to be a researcher at the Institute of Social Sciences. Mr. Chen declined with humility. In the summer of the nineteenth year of the Republic of China (1930), Mr. Chen went to Germany to study German for half a year before returning to France. In March of this year, he suffered from diarrhea and abdominal pain. Doctors diagnosed it as anemia, but later discovered that his lungs and intestines were also affected. He then moved to a sanatorium in the 14th arrondissement of Paris for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he passed away on May 3rd at the young age of twenty-six.

Municipal Zoo Seeks Donations

The Municipal Zoo is planned to be opened at Qinpu, Wenmiao Road. The Municipal Education Bureau has formulated the following measures for soliciting donations of animals, plants, and minerals: (1) The Bureau formulates these measures for soliciting donations of animals, plants, and minerals for the Municipal Zoo. (2) Those who wish to donate various animals such as birds and beasts, fish and insects, various plants such as trees, shrubs, and potted landscapes, and various minerals such as exquisite rocks should first send a letter informing the Bureau of the name, value, and contact address, and the Bureau will send personnel to contact them. (3) For those who donate the aforementioned animals, plants, and minerals, or animal shelters with a value of more than fifty yuan, in addition to the Bureau issuing a receipt and a special nameplate at the display or planting location, a stone tablet will also be erected in the park with an inscription to commemorate them. (4) Those who donate cash may specify the purchase of a certain animal, plant, or mineral for commemoration, and the measures are the same as in Article 3. (5) The measures for those who donate animal, plant, or mineral specimens or models are the same as in Article 3. (6) Those who donate rare items or large amounts of cash will be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 and will also be submitted to the government for awards in accordance with the regulations on donating funds for education. (7) The transportation costs for various animals, plants, minerals, specimens, models, and animal shelters solicited may be borne by the Bureau.
