Free Talk

World Tidbits

—Hai Ke

Astounding Medical Expenses

The King of Siam, suffering from cataracts in his left eye, traveled all the way from Bangkok, Siam, to New York, USA, for medical treatment. He engaged a most famous ophthalmologist to treat him. There are five or six specialist doctors in America whose annual income totals between £100,000 and £150,000. Now, the income of this doctor who is treating the King of Siam’s eye is also similar. And for the sake of serious work, it is bound to abandon other diagnoses, specializing in serving the King of Siam alone, his loss. Of course, the King of Siam has to compensate him. Previously, a wealthy tycoon paid a famous surgeon Mr. So-and-so as much as £50,000 for an operation. So the King of Siam’s expenses will be at least that much. In addition, there are two nurses each for day and night care, an anaesthesia expert, and some assistants, costing about £16,000. The term of treatment is two months. Renting a mansion costs about £60,000. The round-trip travel expenses from Siam to America for the King and Queen and 160 attendants is at least £70,000. Plus all miscellaneous daily expenses, the total is set at £250,000. Therefore, the King of Siam’s medical expenses this time are unprecedented in history. But the monarchs of the East are mostly wealthy, so these medical expenses of £250,000 may not be taken to heart.

Returnee from Hankow Talks of Strange Disaster

— Cheng Zhizheng

This time, the floods in our country have spread to 16 or 17 provinces. Among them, the three towns of Wuhan have suffered the most severe disaster. The details have been repeatedly seen in the newspapers. Yesterday, a friend came to Shanghai from Hankow to avoid the disaster. During our conversation, he told me everything. I selected what the outside world does not know and sent it to this column.

Knee-deep in water in an instant. For more than a month, Hankow has been suffering from heavy rain. However, because the embankment work is very solid, the people are at peace. One morning, my friend went to the market for tea. When he came out an hour later, he heard people saying that the embankment had collapsed. At that time, he still did not believe it. But after walking less than half a mile, he saw water in the barracks of the military police. Before long, a torrent rushed in and was unstoppable. He hurriedly hired a car to return home. The water was already several inches deep. He saw the river water pouring in and quickly rose more than a foot. Only then did he realize that a great disaster was coming, and he could not help but lose his color.

Buried in the belly of fish still in a dream. Many people in Hankow are addicted to opium. Most addicts cannot sleep until early in the morning. The day the dike broke coincided with the morning, and the momentum was fierce, so that some people were swept away by the flood in their sleep. It is said to be tragic.

Rickshaws also have first class. I once saw in a humorous novel that a villager was visiting Shanghai for the first time. When he took a rickshaw, he squatted under the seat, saying that he was sitting in third class. This time, the water level in Hankow rose, and the rickshaw pullers' livelihood was prosperous for a while. Later, as the water level rose, the lower part of the rickshaw was submerged in water. The passengers sat on the hood of the car, which was called first class. When traveling, it was pushed and pulled by two rickshaw pullers, the price was extremely high, and the action was slow. It is also a strange sight. Most of those who do not care about riding in first-class cars can only walk barefoot. However, the water level continued to rise to six or seven feet or even more than a foot. Even first-class cars could not be taken. The suffering can be imagined.

Boats come and go as if entering Venice. After the rickshaws disappeared, they were followed by boats. There were 5,000 boats registered with the municipal government. For a time, the streets became rivers. Boats came and went, as if entering the water city of Venice. The streets were not very wide, and the boats were crowded, colliding from time to time. Each boat needs two boatmen to operate. White flags are inserted on the boats, which is very interesting to look at from a distance.

Easy to go upstairs, difficult to go downstairs. As the water level continues to rise, residents of bungalows can no longer live in peace. They have moved into the most famous five-story hotel in Hankow, hoping to resist the water demon. Unfortunately, it collapsed a few days ago, drowning hundreds of people. As a result, people are afraid to go upstairs again. However, the water in the bungalows is several feet deep, and they cannot sleep peacefully. They are in a dilemma, and their embarrassment can be imagined.

Pouring night soil from the windows. After the flood, the food problem of the citizens caused various difficulties. However, it was also difficult to discharge urine and feces. The municipal government sends boats to collect manure from various places every day. Residents pour it down from the windows of the buildings, mostly into the water, or even on the boatmen. The streets and canals are so unclean, and the bodies are floating on the sea. After a long time, they become foul-smelling. The stronger the sunlight, the more unbearable it becomes. The people of Hankow are really like they are in the eighteenth level of hell.

Famine-stricken victims waiting to be fed. The Pinghan Railway is relatively high, and the victims rely on it as a habitat. However, it has become precarious in recent days. The cries of the victims are unbearable to hear. Now, the relief society sends boats to distribute buns every day. However, there is not enough porridge for many monks, and it is of no avail. If there is no way to retreat the water, the people will perish together. Except for rice shops, which are not allowed to close, and are forced to open, the rest of the city is closed.

Wuchang also becomes a huge flood. When the river water in Hankow entered the city, Wuchang was still safe. Therefore, the relief society had moved some of the victims to Wuchang for temporary residence. However, the dikes in Wuchang also broke after a while, so that there was nothing to do. The wharves of various ships can no longer be seen. It is necessary to rely on boats to board the ships. The ships are extremely crowded. My friend returned in a panic, unable to find a place to sit. Fortunately, the foreign shipping company still has a conscience and has not increased the price.

The failure to repair water conservancy projects has led to huge disasters. Hankow originally had special funds for embankment construction. In recent years, the responsible personnel have been following the same old routine, resulting in an irreversible situation. Although there is a slight punishment now, what will be paid for the sacrifice of thousands of people and the loss of tens of millions of dollars? The people of Hubei will have serious expressions to the Director of the Construction Department.

Special Remuneration

— Chou Cheng

Mr. Zhang Taiyan's son, Zhang Qishi, is only seven years old, but his calligraphy is already elegant and he can write screen strips. This is enough to show the family's academic background. A tiger does not have a dog son. The other day, I went to visit Mr. Taiyan because of something and saw a piece of paper posted in the guest hall with Zhang Qi's writing rules. He does not accept money, but values stationery and toys. It broke the new record of remuneration and is also a good story in the art world. Without naming it, it is called a special lubrication. Here is a special transcription as follows. The four big characters of the writing rules of Shangshu Zhang Qi are written. The middle section is divided into two items: pieces and rewards. (Couplets) A small airplane. Two large notebooks of foreign stationery. A small train. (Screen strips) A Parker fountain pen. (Horizontal scroll) Top-notch a dozen pencils. The four characters "Zhang Qi respectfully ordered" are written below.

Building the Former Residence of Yunlin

— Li Yuyi

Mr. Ni Yunlin was one of the four great painters of the Yuan Dynasty. He lived in Changdaxia, Dongxiang, Wuxi. He was rich and a strong resister of matter. His former residence, Zhituo, now only has a temple. The Qingbi Pavilion, which was once famous at home and abroad for its rich collection of books and paintings, is also nowhere to be found. Only mulberry ridges and rice fields can be seen. However, the legacy of legends is worth recording.

Since ancient times, Yunlin's paintings have been praised for their sparseness, lightness, and remoteness, and are listed as Yi products. Now, looking at the scenery of his residence, tall pines and slender bamboos are planted among the fields. Rivers, streams, and swamps are hidden among the forests. Above, it is reflected in the vast sky and light clouds. Yunlin's sparseness, lightness, and remoteness are also Yunlin's sparseness, lightness, and remoteness. It is natural and there is no doubt.

Mr. Yunlin loved tung trees and washed them every day. The wild old man passed on words that his tung tree was spit on by an immortal, so the tung juice is still sticky today. Beside his former residence, there is a dead tree like an ape. The villagers said that it must be inhabited by gods because it has not rotted for a long time.

In front of it, there is a short stream called Xiazhao River. The water quality is 20% heavier than other places, just like Huiquan. It is clear and bottomless. The snails produced are all covered with silky green hair. Further ahead, there are two ancient pines, like the Six Dynasties pines of Zhongda and Mao. All of these are named after Mr.

The farmers in his residence are all named Ni, totaling hundreds of families. Regardless of wealth or poverty, the house style is to build a wide hall in the three-entry house. There are nineteen plaques of chastity and filial piety on the hall. And it is not surprising to have two or three parties. The custom of women keeping festival is a strange thing.

I worked at the factory's aesthetic appreciation society at the home of my close friend Mr. Ni Xiaoqian. I saw that there were also two plaques in his hall. It turns out that two generations of his ancestors have kept their chastity. From this, it can be inferred that there are more women than men in that place and they are healthy. It is said in our country that the rich give birth to more daughters and the poor give birth to more sons. Based on today's statistical research, it is also confirmed. The reason why there are so many women in that place is because of its wealth. In addition to rice, wheat, and miscellaneous grains, the benefits of sericulture are added. Silkworms can be raised in spring and autumn. The old and young have their own duties. Chaste women concentrate their efforts on this. Life is abundant and there is no other thought. And keeping festival and being good can reduce fertility, which is beneficial to the population problem. For thousands of years, hundreds of families with the surname Ni have not been overcrowded. It can be used as proof. As for Yunlin's paintings, those who get natural are not only inspired by the scenery.

His affluent life, with enough food and clothing, is the biggest cause of art. Or, it is thought that the essence of art comes from a strong spirit. Would it be delusional to think of this?

Travelogue of India (93)

— Linghua

All young children are nurtured in their mother's embrace and grow up by their mother's hand. From the womb, they are raised by the holy spirit, and as they grow, they are constantly protected, forming a second nature. How difficult it is for women to separate from the divine, and how difficult it is to eradicate worldly religions. Observing the waters of the Ganges, I recall the King of Persia's words to the Buddha in the Surangama Sutra: "I remember at the age of three, my loving mother took me to visit the Jiva God and see the waters of the Ganges." This confirms that Indians are nurtured in the embrace of the divine, hence their deep sense of gratitude towards their mothers. On the way back from the Ganges, I saw many women holding children, all with foreheads marked with five colors, commemorating their baptism in the holy water.

We passed many small temples, all guarded by women. Pilgrims come to offer incense and give money. I don't know if they are female nuns or not. But from what I know, there are three irresistible forces in the world: power, money, and love between the sexes. All are difficult to resist. Although Hinduism is extremely profound and far-reaching, cases of its monks having illegitimate children, returning to secular life, or engaging in love affairs are frequently seen and still require lawyers to resolve. Each temple has monks and also women, who are said to be their disciples. But in reality, many cases occur. I have read widely in religious history and know that talking about principles too high and not in accordance with human life is bound to fail. This is why the monastic system is an exception and difficult to be the norm. We passed a large park, magnificently structured with beautiful flowers and plants.

At 5 p.m. that afternoon, I lectured at the Anglo-Bengalee Intermediate College, Allahabad, a joint university of two provinces. The vice-principal, Mr. Asthana, presided, and there were only about a hundred listeners. In India, large gatherings of thousands or even tens of thousands of people are very common. This proves that the Buddha's sermons with eighteen thousand disciples present are not exaggerated, as some Chinese think. Such large gatherings are still commonly seen in India. Indians' love of learning and wisdom is worthy of being the first teachers and leaders in the world. The small number of listeners today was because the lecture was announced only three hours before it started, students had already dispersed for the New Year, and it was also a market closing day, with Gandhi's followers engaged in a major national movement. Asthana is a famous person in the province, and many students asked me questions, all of which I was able to answer. Their love of learning is admirable. Before I finished my lecture, Gandhi's followers were shouting slogans on the street outside, parading through the city. The lights were already on. Around 6 p.m., the meeting ended, and I followed the crowd to observe Gandhi's movement. Men and women came in single file, holding Indian flags of various sizes, or carrying wooden sticks, or with lit lamps on their heads, or with incense. The men wore Gandhi caps, made of coarse white cloth, slightly pointed in the front, exactly like the large white mourning caps in China. There was no difference at all. They went to a large park that could hold thirty to forty thousand people, shouting loudly with tears in their eyes, because their relatives and children had been harmed in prison. I don't understand Indian languages, but hearing their voices, even now as I write this, I can't help but feel sorrow for them. The women's speeches were particularly inspiring. In Allahabad alone, there were 30,000 people participating in the movement. I heard that in every city and town across India, large and small, similar movements were taking place today. It can be said to be a magnificent sight. Indians regard Gandhi as a living Buddha today. An Indian told me that the British dare not harm Gandhi. If they did, a major riot would erupt, and it could immediately turn into a communist-style revolution. If they use gentleness, the Indians might still be able to tolerate it.

Random Notes on a Northeast Inspection Tour (4)

— Liu Suiqiu

(5) The Origin of the Siku Quanshu in the Wensu Pavilion

During Emperor Qianlong's inspection tours, the Wensu Pavilion was established in Shenyang to house the Siku Quanshu (Complete Library of the Four Treasuries). Today, Fengtian (Shenyang) still possesses a complete copy of the Siku Quanshu, a gift from the Qing Emperor's eastern tour. The front part of the current Wensu Pavilion serves as the location of the Liaoning Provincial Education Association. To visit the Siku Quanshu, one must obtain permission and an introduction from the association or the provincial government. This spring, I accompanied Mr. Wang Huayi, the vice-chairman of the association, to browse through it once. I heard someone say that Fengtian had planned to reprint the Siku Quanshu a few years ago and had already printed a sample in Western-style binding. The Secretary-General of the European League of Nations, Mr. Eric Drummond, was willing to undertake the sale of many copies and requested to see the sample. Upon seeing the Western-style binding, he was displeased and directly told Zhang Xueliang that Westerners did not like this type of binding. Later, due to other reasons, the project was shelved.

(6) Imperial Literary Works

Another byproduct of the Qing emperors' inspection tours to Shenyang is the Shengjing Fu (Ode to Shengjing), an imperial literary work. Last year, I had the opportunity to see Emperor Qianlong's edition in the Fengtian Library. Upon inspection, the content of the Shengjing Fu written by Emperor Qianlong consists of thirty-two types of seal script in Chinese and thirty-two types of seal script in Manchu. The library has eight sets of thirty-two volumes in Chinese and eight sets of twenty-five volumes in Manchu. The thirty-two types of Chinese seal script are:

1. Jade Chopstick Seal Script 2. Curious Character Seal Script 3. Greater Seal Script 4. Lesser Seal Script

5. Upper Greater Seal Script 6. Hanging Needle Seal Script 7. Sui Script Seal Script 8. Willow Leaf Seal Script

9. Inverted Leek Seal Script 10. Revolving Constellation Seal Script 11. Lingzhi Seal Script 12. Biluo Seal Script

13. Hanging Dew Seal Script 14. Dragon Script Seal Script 15. Hanging Cloud Seal Script 16. Tadpole Script

17. Bird Track Seal Script 18. Insect Carving Seal Script 19. Qilin Script Seal Script 20. Swan Head Seal Script

21. Bird Script Seal Script 22. Luan Phoenix Seal Script 23. Dou Script Seal Script 24. Dragon Claw Seal Script

25. Scissors Seal Script 26. Tassel Dropping Seal Script 27. Suspended Needle Seal Script 28. Shu Script

29. Gold Inlay Seal Script 30. Talisman Carving Seal Script 31. Flying White Script 32. Zhongding Seal Script

The entire ode was translated into French by the Jesuit priest Amiot in 1770 and published in Paris. It is mentioned in the Moukden entry of the Encyclopedia Britannica. I also had the opportunity to browse through the French translation at the library. The library has many books and illustrations related to the history of northeastern China, as well as various Chinese steles and rubbings from past dynasties. The Japanese are not only involved in politics, economy, military affairs, and industry in Manchuria and Mongolia.

(7) The Wealth of Chinese Maps and Provincial and County Gazetteers

I still remember last winter when Mr. Liang from the Academia Sinica was dispatched to Rehe (Jehol) for archaeological research. When he passed through Fengtian, he wanted to find a detailed map of Rehe but could not. On November 7th of the same year, I received a letter from Mr. Matsuzaki Tsuruo, the head of the Chinese section of the Dalian Library, inviting me to visit the Chinese map exhibition held by the library and enclosing a catalog. The collection includes 451 types of detailed maps of all provinces and counties in China, even remote areas, some dating back two or three hundred years. I had already previewed these maps at the Dalian Library earlier. I also heard that the library has complete and unparalleled provincial and county gazetteers of all provinces in China, as well as many other ancient and rare books. When I visited the library in Dalian in the past, the librarian, Mr. Kakinuma Kai, showed me a catalog of the library's collection, about six inches thick. He kindly gifted me the first and second volumes of the printed catalog. The retail price for each volume is about two Japanese yen. I heard that there is also a non-public catalog.

The Current Situation of the Yarn, Cotton, and Yarn Markets is Good

The yarn market has turned firmer, trending slightly higher. Overseas cotton and yarn conditions are rising consistently, and the rise in Toyo's three grades of yarn is exceptionally strong. As a result, the market sentiment is excited, and buying interest is tighter. However, the large firms' open positions have not yet been offset, so the market sentiment is still stable. Most small merchants are mentally exhausted, as they are disappointed in the autumn sales due to the severe floods in all directions. However, there is a slight hope for a turnaround in foreign cotton.

The Cotton Market is Inclined to the Upper Reaches

The cotton market is trending upward. American cotton is rising, and Japanese Dongmian is buying in. Most local cotton merchants are in a long position, and their pulling force is particularly strong when they encounter an opportunity. As for the issue of standard cotton including Indian cotton, both sides are still discussing it. There are rumors in the business community that there were floods in all directions this year, and Hankou suffered particularly heavy losses. In the future, it will inevitably be subject to squeezing, so most people are buying in to go long. However, looking back at the world cotton industry, it is still in surplus. All factories' current cotton transactions show no signs of movement, so the future still depends on American cotton for ups and downs.

Hankou Standard Rises Six or Seven Cents. At the opening of the Hankou standard cotton market in the morning, both American and Indian cotton rose, and there were fewer merchants in the market. Prices for various months rose by 3 cents. In the afternoon, Japanese merchants bought in, and the market became even tighter. Prices for various months rose by 2.5 to 3 cents. A total of 78,400 dan were traded. It was found that Dachang sold 2,100 dan, Shenda 2,700 dan, Yichang 2,900 dan, Xinheng 1,600 dan, and Shenchang 1,500 dan. Guangfeng bought 4,100 dan, Changfeng 4,200 dan, Deji 2,300 dan, and Yuda 200 dan each. The closing prices are recorded on the left.

Hankou Standard Closing Prices, Gains and Losses, and Open Interest. December 34.35, up 60, 173.400 October 34.40, up 70, 153.600 January 34.35, 55, 216.400 November 34.50, 65, 181.300

Spot Demand is Cut Off. The current cotton business is cut off. All factories are watching from the sidelines.

Foreign Cotton and Yarn Rise Consistently

American Cotton Resists Shorts and Rises. Yesterday, American cotton rose due to short covering. The harvest conditions were poor, there was a lack of merchants, and it was firm. Futures rose by 14 to 18 points, and spot rose by 20 points. British cotton futures rose by 6 points, and spot rose by 3 points. Egyptian cotton spot was unchanged. Indian cotton was firm due to Gandhi's decision to attend the London conference. Pingguoer rose by 1 rupee, Omula rose by 1.25 rupees, and Bailuoxi rose by 1 rupee. The original telegram is recorded on the left (telegram on the 27th).

The Osaka Spot Yarn Rises Again by Three or Four Yuan. The Osaka spot yarn telegram: 20 count Blue Fish, 117 yuan, up 3 yuan, corresponding to Shanghai regulations 195 taels 40 cents. 20 count Red God of Wealth, 110 yuan, up 4 yuan, corresponding to Shanghai regulations 183 taels 70 cents. 20 count Red God of Wealth, 106 yuan, up 2 yuan, corresponding to Shanghai regulations 177 taels. 16 count Three Horses, 106 yuan, up 2 yuan, corresponding to Shanghai regulations 177 taels. The Rice Market in Hexia Rose and Fell Again

The storm in Nanshi stopped yesterday morning. Twenty or thirty ships of goods arrived from the interior. Sales in urban and rural stores also slackened. The situation turned loose due to the dispatch of investigators by the Social Affairs Bureau, and the market sentiment calmed down. Changxi Beigeng temporarily maintained its original price. Sales of Su Tong Ping Li and other goods were weak, and the price was short by three corners. Early and late rice arrived and sold equally. Inventories were thick, falling by five corners. Luxiang Jian goods were also scattered, and if they were removed, they would move slightly. The market showed a steady trend. There was no market for new geng and changed yin yuan due to a lack of goods.

Not many goods arrived at Xinzha yesterday because the weather was clear. Sales on the street were sluggish. Thick geng, medium and second grades, were all tired by seven corners, and buying interest was extremely weak. Everyone in the market was looking to go lower. Although the supply of thin rice was limited, and the outbound routes were not good, the price also fell by 1 yuan. Changed yin yuan went downstream due to the strong arrival of geng rice, affecting new geng and foreign tips. There was no price increase or decrease. Luxiang tips and Bu tips were clearly stable and secretly weak. Foreign rice arrivals gradually thinned, and merchant gangs were actively buying, with prices continuing to be soft by two or three corners.

Small Compressing Newly Set at 3,000 Tons

1,000 Tons of Repatriated Goods Traded...Northern Gang Handles and Loads Passenger Yuan Rice Yesterday, spot transactions of foreign rice were suspended, but futures were very active. Spot merchants asked for high prices due to low inventories, but entrants intended to suppress smaller prices and handle them again due to the fall in flour and wheat, so there were no transactions. In futures, Dafeng sold 1,000 tons of repatriated goods, which were small compreesing for September, priced at 6 taels 5 cents and 2 fen. They were originally thrown out by the Taihe Foreign Firm. New transactions of foreign rice included 3,000 tons of small compressing for November, which was also the approved reply to the telegram sent by Xiangmao the day before yesterday. After this batch was traded, market sentiment slightly softened.

期麥晨跌午回

Yesterday's wheat market, after the morning opening, prices for each month fell because the National Government announced the import of fifteen million bushels of American wheat. The news inevitably shook market confidence. The current month, due to delivery considerations, saw no buying interest from factories, and prices dropped to a low of 3.72 taels. September fell to 3.94 taels, October to 4.03 taels, November to 4.07 taels, and December to 4.11 taels. January fell to 4.14 taels, a drop of three to six fen compared to the previous day. However, in the afternoon opening, there was active short covering from outside investors, and the flour market rebounded, boosting prices for forward months by three to four fen. The delivery volume for the current month is said to have reached over one hundred carts of sampled goods. If dealers do not roll over their positions, it will likely reach two hundred carts (it is reported that Xiangxin received fifty carts, Shenda over twenty carts, and Xinfeng twenty to thirty carts). As a result, the current month was two fen higher than the previous day, September was one fen higher, October remained unchanged, November was down one fen, December down two fen, and January unchanged. Spot wheat saw no transactions due to lack of interest from factories.

標粉受美麥影響

後市補空稍回

Yesterday’s flour market, after the morning opening, prices for each month saw drops due to the announcement that the National Government had approved the import of fifteen million bushels of American wheat for disaster relief. This news shook market confidence, as the massive American aid implied no fear of food shortages. The long positions seemed to have lost a guarantee, so selling pressure came from factories. The current month fell to a low of 2.0775 taels, September to 2.0875 taels, and October to 2.107 taels. Other months also fell, with an average drop of two to three fen. However, in the afternoon opening, the market initially remained weak, but rapid short covering and a slight increase in spot sales helped stabilize the market. But generally speaking, this large drop followed by a small recovery is not a good sign. As a result, the current month was up by five li, September and October were up by one fen, November was up by 1.25 li, December by one fen, and January by 1.5 fen.

Sugar Market: Quiet Trading, Flat Prices

Granulated White Sugar Shows Slight Firming

Yesterday's sugar market saw reports from producing regions that Cuban spot sugar was priced at 1.4375, New York sugar futures for September and December were both priced at 1.31, and May and September of next year were priced at 1.35 and 1.41 respectively, a drop of three to seven fen compared to previous reports. Java spot and futures sugar prices remained unchanged. The public market saw little trading, but market sentiment was relatively stable. Dutch No. 24 coarse granulated white new sugar was traded at a price increase of 11.65 taels, with the market appearing firm. No. 20 medium granulated white sugar was priced at 11 taels, with few interested buyers. Tai Koo sugar transactions were also sluggish. B mark was 12.025 taels, DY mark was 11.825 taels, HX mark was 11.75 taels, HM mark was 11.4 taels, and O mark was 9.4 taels, trending flat. Huaxin CW mark was 11.9 taels, with little interest. Some old oil-bag coarse granulated white sugar was sold for 11.45 taels for a few hundred bags. Dealers showed little interest, and the market appeared listless.

North-South Goods: Large Quantities of New Black Melon Seeds Arrive

Market Strengthens Instead

A small quantity of new black melon seeds had arrived in previous batches, with Jiangxi seeds priced at 16 taels and Tianjin seeds at 17 taels. It is now reported that wholesale grocers have received a large quantity of new Xu Kui seeds, 1,200 bags in total. Because asking prices were too high, no deals have been made, and both parties are currently holding out. However, there are also 2,000 bags of Tianjin seeds that may arrive, making it difficult for prices to fall. Due to the floods this year, most producing areas are reporting reduced harvests, and people are optimistic, so sellers will definitely be firm, which can be stated with certainty.

Silk & Tea: Japanese Merchants Continue to Purchase Shanghai Silk

Yesterday's silk market in Shanghai remained unchanged. European and American markets offered lower prices for Japanese silk, with a difference of over 200 taels compared to Shanghai white silk. There were no changes in silk telegraph rates. Only Japanese firms continued to cover short positions, with Mitsui and others buying 40 bales of Shanghai white silk, and Dachang and others buying 20 bales of dried white silk, with prices remaining firm.

無錫白絲頭運滬不弱

180 Pieces of Wuxi White Silk Waste Shipped to Shanghai, Market is Strong

Of the 48 silk factories in Wuxi, 40 are currently operating. The output of silk waste has increased. As the end of the month approaches, factories need to deliver silk waste to foreign firms. Yesterday, 180 pieces of long-fibered cocoon silk, boiled cocoon silk, and other types of silk waste from Wuxi silk factories arrived in Shanghai by passenger train, in preparation for delivery.

婺源珍眉歐銷轉暢

Wuyuan Zhenmei Green Tea Sales to Europe Improve

Yesterday, the tea market in Shanghai saw improved sales of Wuyuan high-grade Zhenmei green tea by foreign firms such as Xiechang, Yongxing, Baochang, and Dutoit. Tunxi Zhenmei tea was also slightly favored by the Jinlong Foreign Firm, with a firm price of 150-160 taels. Other varieties such as Gongxi Needle-eyebrow and Xiu-eyebrow teas were also actively traded. The green tea market has stabilized. Qimen black tea was favored by firms such as Jardine Matheson and Tienshsiang, but the selling price fell to 40-50 taels, causing significant losses for Chinese tea merchants.

Piece Goods Market Remains Sluggish

The piece goods market has weakened again, showing no sign of recovery. This is mainly due to the severe floods in various ports, causing widespread damage, which has completely halted sales to customers. In addition, the anti-Japanese sentiment remains high, making Japanese goods extremely sluggish. As a result, the cotton cloth public market has seen unprecedentedly low trading volume in recent days. Yesterday, medium and fine cotton cloth fell again, with Blue Double Fish at 7.4 taels, Yang Crane Colorful Ball at 7.35 taels, and Balloon at 7.7 taels. However, fine twill remained firm, as dyeing mills in Sichuan had strong demand. Coarse cloth continued to fall by 2.5 to 5 fen, and coarse twill was sluggish. Japanese goods have seen only sporadic sales recently, with small quantities being shipped to places such as Sichuan, Henan, Yunnan, and Guizhou by postal parcel. Among these, Snowflake Serge was more popular, with Hanshan Temple at 3.2 taels, Qianliju at 3.15 taels, and Filial Piety at 3.175 taels. Snowflake-colored Ting was also being shipped, with the Great Wall Horse-Riding Official Promotion design at a uniform price of 2.95 taels. Yuehua Velvet, Zhigong Ni, and Zhigong Satin have been declining sharply in recent days due to sluggish demand, down by about five li compared to last week. Sales of both arriving and stored Western goods have been quiet. The plain foreign yarn stored in Shanghai was largely damaged by the recent floods.

Metal Goods: More Declines Than Gains

Recent metal goods trading has been exceptionally quiet due to limited procurement from various regions, resulting in more declines than gains in market prices. Given the current frequent floods and sluggish cargo, it is difficult to expect a prosperous metal market. According to insiders, significant market improvement is unlikely until after the Mid-Autumn Festival.

Encouraging Items: New Lead Wire: After the boycott of Japanese goods, Western goods prices have increased significantly, estimated at 13.5 taels per picul (No. 16 to No. 20), while No. 21 to No. 25 sold for 19 taels. Yesterday, due to lack of inventory, 18-gauge black iron sheet also rose to 11.5 taels. 7.5 li British steel plate has risen to 6.5 taels, another increase of one qian. Garden lead wire is in short supply, and the price has risen to 5.25 taels. White lead sheet, red copper, and spot tin have seen active trading, but prices remain stable without significant gains.

Falling Items: Tinplate: There is little trading, and there is no hope of price recovery. It is fortunate that the market can hold steady. French West nails are currently estimated at 8.75 taels, but there are no buyers. American white iron sheet is becoming oversupplied and weakening, currently estimated at 18.75 taels. Except for the Fujian merchants, no other merchants are showing interest, so prices may continue to decline. White lead sheet is also softening due to a lack of sales orders. After the influx of domestic lead, the market for green lead is even more sluggish, estimated at 15.75 taels, with very few buyers. Other items such as new foreign coins, bamboo-joint steel, and new iron wire are all showing signs of weakness.

Youth Garden

In Memory of My Late Friend, Mr. Chen Xing Shu, and an Introduction to His Thoughts (Continued)

— (He Ting, sent from Paris)

Whether collectivism is the truth is another question, which we cannot discuss here. However, the motivation behind this utterly selfless theory is already worthy of our admiration. We can see his selfless spirit even more clearly from his attitude towards friends.

Xing Shu was a kind and lovable friend. His friendship was very deep and sincere. However, he never let personal feelings interfere with public justice. Many people in society make friends for the purpose of mutual flattery and forming alliances for jobs. Xing Shu hated this the most. He believed that one should not work solely for oneself or one's friends. In a China riddled with sores and filled with the cries of suffering people, one sees compatriots in hunger, cold, poverty, and sickness everywhere. How many talents, how many patriots, how many people capable of hard work are buried within? Why and how can we always be fortunate people? If we open our eyes wide and look at society, how can we bear to hope only for the happiness of ourselves and our friends? China's problem is that everyone helps their friends but does not find ways to help society.

But the Chinese, who are accustomed to living in a feudal society, only know private relationships and do not know public justice. The so-called "heroes," "good men," "patriots," and "knights" in society are all figures who use public office for private gain, take bribes to help friends, and cultivate cliques. Who knows that there is a society beyond private relationships? Society and public justice seem too abstract to them. Who can understand this? No wonder, the more friends there are, the more brothers there are, the more developed private friendships are, the worse social undertakings become day by day. "Friends" and "comrades" will become synonyms for partners in robbery. In today's society, who would be willing to consider Xing Shu's idea of not harming the public for private gain?

One day, on a Sunday, many friends were together chatting and relaxing. Politics came up, and everyone complained and sighed as usual. Because students studying abroad have the most complaints, and the reasons for their complaints are also the most complicated. Xing Shu did not approve of complaining. He said, "When we observe society, we don't need to be happy or sad about the ups and downs of political tides, because political tides are only superficial waves in society and not the main source that drives social evolution. When discussing matters, we must trace the root and source. We must change our perspective and focus on the fundamental problem of society: the problem of production."

Here, his views are quite close to historical materialism, although he was not a believer in historical materialism. He analyzed the source of social chaos based on social production. He believed that Chinese society had lost its economic balance. The living standards in rural areas and the living standards in big cities were too different. The people in rural areas were living the economic life of Europe in the 16th and 17th centuries, while the people in big cities were enjoying the most luxurious material civilization of the 20th century. But most of the people in big cities can only consume. They are either "landlords," "compradors," or bureaucrats, all of whom do not engage in direct production and are "fed by others." They all directly or indirectly rely on the poor, cold, hungry, and uneducated small farmers, laborers, and small businessmen in rural areas and cities to maintain their lives. Under such circumstances, it is no wonder that the social economy is deteriorating day by day, and the people's livelihoods are becoming more and more painful. Without a solid economic foundation, it is difficult to have political stability in society. Therefore, if we want social stability, we must work hard to produce.

What a fundamental principle this is! From a sociological perspective, society loses "balance" and becomes unable to survive. Chinese society, from all aspects, has lost its balance and is in a state of "conflict" and "contradiction." In the economic aspect, there is an imbalance between the rural economy and the urban economy, an imbalance between consumption and production, and an uneven distribution between direct producers and indirect producers. In terms of morality and thought, there are conflicts between new and old cultures and between Eastern and Western cultures. Not to mention society, even an individual's thoughts and behaviors - of course, partly a reflection of society - are all in conflict, contradiction, and disorder. Therefore, political disorder has its main causes. What is the use of our sighing and lamenting? Xing Shu can be said to understand the source of China's social ills.

Now we must talk about his professional views. He was one of the best among the students studying abroad. He naturally wanted to be a scholar and professor, and a famous one. But he often said to people that he did not want to be a professor or scholar, because this was not the most urgent career needed in today's society. He really wanted to run a small business. Friends often laughed at his fantasies when they heard this, but this was indeed his very serious idea. Because he lived in the foothills, he had thought of many ways to cultivate the mountains and drafted many plans to promote the planting of fruit trees. If we think of his words as an Eastern-style hermit idea, we would be wrong. Xing Shu was an active person, at least in his thinking, because he had not yet acted. He was not a pessimist, nor was he seeking personal comfort and elegance. He saw the needs of society and advocated production, so he himself was willing to be a pioneer and carry out production activities. If big businesses fail, then work hard at small jobs.

The millennia-old concept of valuing scholars ("those who labor with their minds govern others, those who labor with their strength are governed by others") has made the Chinese see the terms "reading," "scholar," "learning," and "culture" as too mysterious. Who knows that culture and learning are just tools to increase the happiness of life, and have no value in themselves? From Xing Shu's professional views, we can know that his thoughts had completely shed the stench of "scholar-officials." If Xing Shu had not died young, whether his ideas could have been realized would certainly have been a major question. But the fact that he could advocate this way already meant that he was not a scholar who simply echoed others.

If the Chinese nation does not perish from this, in the near future, there will certainly be many patriots and young people who abandon their books, leave their purely theoretical laboratories, and race towards the path of production. The trend of social evolution is already forcing us to run that way. Xing Shu's theory is indeed a practical theory and a product of the needs of today's society.

I have introduced Xing Shu's main thoughts to everyone. I have not embellished them. I am not here to praise a dead friend. This is just a partial record of many late-night talks between me and Xing Shu in the six months since he returned to France from Germany. It's just a pity that my pen is too clumsy, my heart is too coarse, and my temperament is different from Xing Shu's. There are no major discrepancies between my descriptions and the gist of what he said, but there must be many differences in tone and wording. This is something I myself feel very dissatisfied with. However, there is no other way. Strictly speaking, one person cannot represent another person's thoughts.

There are really too many things about Xing Shu that are worth remembering. Everything about him is worth remembering. However, I have to stop writing for now. If I keep talking, I will never finish, and it will always be too tragic.

Neither nature nor society has ever been rationalized. In the natural world, how many beautiful flowers are destroyed by storms when they are in full bloom? In society, how many intelligent and hardworking people are permanently buried because they lack a suitable environment for cultivation? Nature gave Xing Shu innate intelligence and a favorable environment, but then took away his physical health. This is truly the unkindness of heaven and earth. I do not lament for Xing Shu; what difference is there between life and death? I only lament for society.

Editor's Note: Mr. Chen Xing Shu was one of the founders of Guanghua University and once held a teaching position at Guanghua University. In 1927, he went to France to study political economy at the University of Paris. He was expected to obtain his doctorate this summer, but unexpectedly, he suffered from peritonitis and died in Paris on May 3rd. Now, Mr. Chen's friends, such as He Bingsong and Pan Gongzhan, have scheduled a memorial meeting to be held on the 30th of this month at the South China Science Society on Albert Road, Rue Sieyeshams, in the French Concession.

The Lindbergh Family's Background and Early Life

— Yuan Baokang

One

I was born on February 4, 1902, in Detroit, Michigan, USA. At that time, my father was practicing law at Littelfos in Minneapolis. Less than two months after my birth, my father took me to a farm on the banks of the Mississippi River, which was only two miles away from Littelfos.

My father's name was Charles Lindbergh (Note: In the United States, it is very common for fathers and sons to have the same name. You only need to add a "(Senior)" or "(Junior)" after the name.) He was born on January 20, 1860, in Stockholm, Sweden. My grandfather was Mårten Olsson (Note: After immigrating to the United States, he changed his last name to Lindbergh). He served as a member of parliament and secretary to the emperor in Sweden.

In 1860, my grandfather led his family and took a ship from Sweden to the United States. Soon after, he built a house in Sauk Centre, which is next to Minneapolis. My father spent his childhood there.

Two

At that time, there were few schools established in Minnesota. Therefore, my father spent most of his childhood hunting and fishing. As for education, he mostly received it at home. Occasionally, he was able to attend a village school, but he never finished a semester.

When he formally received education, he was still studying at the Grof Lake High School in Minneapolis. After graduating, he was admitted to the University of Michigan, where he also obtained a Bachelor of Laws degree. After graduating from university, he immediately returned to Littelfos to practice law. However, he soon turned his attention to politics. In 1906, in the 10th Congress, my father was elected as the representative of the 6th district of Minnesota and sent to Washington to attend the meeting. He held this position for a total of ten years.

My mother was English and was born in Detroit. She also graduated from the University of Michigan with a Bachelor of Science degree. Later, she obtained a Master's degree from Columbia University. My maternal grandfather was Charles Land, a dentist in Detroit. He was born in New Cross, Canada. My maternal great-grandfather was John Land, who immigrated to Canada from England and was one of the founders of Hamilton City.

My maternal grandfather devoted himself to dental research and worked tirelessly in the laboratory all day long. He made great contributions to dentistry, such as the inlay of gold teeth. He was also the first to invent and use porcelain teeth. Therefore, many people called him the ancestor of porcelain teeth. Presumably, this honor was hard-earned.

Before I was four years old, I lived in Minneapolis. Apart from going to Detroit, I had not traveled far to other places. After my father was elected, our family had two addresses. We spent the winters in Washington and returned to Minnesota in the summers. Detroit also became a place that we often passed through.

At the age of eight, I entered Force School in Washington. Because our movements were uncertain, it affected my studies. As a result, I never finished a full school year.

During this period, I made long journeys, crossing the United States twice and going to Panama once. But these interesting long journeys never satisfied my desires, because I am a very good traveler.

Among the subjects in school, my favorite was mechanics. After graduating from Littelfos High School, I decided to study mechanics. Two years later, I transferred to the Mechanical Engineering College of the University of Wisconsin in Madison.

After that, I turned my attention to aviation. The first time I saw an airplane was in Washington in 1912. Since then, my heart has been bewitched by it. In 1922, I entered an aviation school. Although I was surrounded by airplanes every day, it never satisfied me, because I felt that I had too little contact with airplanes.

Four

The busyness of university studies caused me to often suffer from headaches. I had no choice but to read outdoors to avoid the pain.

During my first summer vacation, I went to the artillery school in Kentucky. After staying for about two weeks, I scraped together $40 and set off on a motorcycle for Florida. When I arrived at Jacksonville, I didn't overspend. On the same day, I took the same motorcycle and sought another way back. Seventeen days later, I returned to Madison, with the motorcycle damaged and only nine dollars left in my pocket. I rested in Madison for a while, and the motorcycle was heavily repaired. When it was finished, I took the road back to Littelfos to spend the remaining vacation.

In the third semester, I decided to study aviation and decided that this should be the direction of my student life. Therefore, before the end of the semester, around mid-March (1922), I resolutely left Madison and went to Lincoln, entering the Nebraska Aviation Training School. At this point, my long-cherished wish can be said to have been achieved. When I left school, many people clicked their tongues and said that I was young and reckless, abandoning the right path and turning to evil. But thinking about it now, my success today is entirely based on that decisive action at that time.

Translator's Note: Mr. and Mrs. Lindbergh are currently making a flight to the Far East and are about to arrive in Tokyo. The political circles in our country are also preparing a welcome meeting. Deputy Commander Zhang is now willing to provide his personal Ford plane for them to tour China. Therefore, before they arrive in the country, I am introducing their history here.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

A Woman's Confession

— Xu Gengsheng

A Woman's Confession Xu Gengsheng

Zhou Leshan has achieved astonishing success in using fresh and lively brushstrokes, outlining concisely, swiftly, and yet with rich and delicate colors, to depict the lives, thoughts, and actions of modern urban women, which forms the foundation of most of his creations.

(A Woman's Confession) includes a total of fifteen short stories and one novella, namely A Woman's Confession. This piece can be considered the representative work of this collection because it best reflects the author's style (that concise and deeply moving style). From the preface by Mr. Chuan Yanzhang.

The so-called A Woman's Confession depicts a woman's confession before her death. This woman had been married to seven husbands, had wandered through famous cities such as Dalian, Nanyang, Kuala Lumpur, Paris, and Shanghai. She had been a child bride (adopted daughter-in-law), and then became a modern girl, a dancer, a singer, the wife of an official, a famous actor, a school principal, a wealthy merchant, and a lawyer, and finally became a prostitute and the owner of a brothel. Despite such complex plots, characters, vast regions, and disparate customs, the author has managed to include her within twenty-eight Chinese pages, making us feel that every plot is vividly portrayed, all the characters are distinct, and every region is like a personal experience. This cannot but be recognized as the author's mental agility.

The female protagonist, Wei, is a bold and willful woman, courageous in love and contention, but easily subdued, intoxicated, and captivated by love, a woman of strong character. Let us look at the words of our author when her second husband, Y, falls in love with her classmate, Miss B, and (takes Miss B under his arm and sends her out the door), describing her state of mind in contending for love:

(At that time, I wanted to commit suicide, and I also wanted to take revenge. Suicide, revenge, I thought about it all night, and finally decided that suicide is the act of the weak. I decided to take revenge.

After embracing the doctrine of revenge, my actions were completely different from before. My social activities outside were all kept secret from Y. At that time, I expected Y to be particularly good to me, and Y gradually began to love me wholeheartedly again. One night, he voluntarily confessed to me his previous sins. He said that he didn't know why his conscience was temporarily blinded and he was seduced by B.

He wanted me to forgive him. I pretended not to care about it and said with a smile,

"Does this count as anything? Young people often have this."

I then proceeded with my revenge plan.

I started to attack Chen Butong, a good friend of Y's…)

Let's look again at the place where she is depicted as bold and willful. This is a scene of her divorce from her third husband, Chen Butong:

(Why did you engage in singing opera without my consent?

I coldly replied to him,

Can you control me? Is acting in a play an illegitimate business?

I will not allow you to go on stage today no matter what.

I insist on going on stage, what can you do?

His face turned green and he shouted loudly,

If you don't listen to me, then we will sever our relationship from now on.

Really?

Who's joking with you? I don't want a woman like you who doesn't listen to restrictions.

Then that's for the best. Meet me at Lawyer Lu's office after my performance.)

Let's take another look at how he writes about her being subdued, intoxicated, and captivated by love. This is her cohabitation with Ying Baiyi in Dalian:

(At that time, I had found true love in the world. I began to believe that the saying "love is unconditional" could be established.)

At that time, what did I hope for? I only hoped that my and Baiyi's happy life would continue forever, to infinity.)

As for the personalities of the several male characters in the story, they are also clearly different. Wei's older brother is a deep and decisive person. Y is a young man whose love easily drifts. Chen Butong is a copper-smelling merchant, in whose eyes everything is commodified, and women are also commodified. Wu Baiyi is a strong male, and at the same time loyal to the physical fascination of women. Yao Yicheng is a generous merchant, and therefore also a cowardly husband. Huang Fang is a feminine man, a fatalist without decision. Chen Yi'ou is an insidious person. Xia Weiyin is a dashing artist. Mr. C is a silent lawyer with a scientific mind. Although the temperaments of the above-mentioned people are all different, the author did not deliberately portray them from the front. He only hinted from the side, subtly, unintentionally, and set them off from all aspects. Apart from the depiction of Mr. C's character, this is also an expression of the author's rich artistic cultivation.

In addition, I want to talk about his skill in writing scenery. I will bring up his writing about Paris here. Paris is a famous city with a high degree of material life in the world, but if you first focus on the material, then no matter how you write (gold-obsessed and paper-drunk,) you cannot show the characteristics of Paris, you cannot show the lively and fresh Paris. The author seems to have seen this, so he specially extracts the suburbs of Paris to write, extracts the autumn of Paris to write, and from the autumn, he extracts the red leaves to write. Thus, the red leaves of autumn in the suburbs of Paris are written so concretely, so vividly, so humorously, and so full of poetic interest. Now let's quote her below:

(When I arrived in Paris, it was just autumn. The autumn in Paris is more beautiful than anything else. If you look out to the suburbs of Paris, the mountains and fields are covered with red leaves, red enough to be loved. At that time, the suburbs were more lively than the city. Fashionable women often took their lovers in light cars and went for a stroll nearby. That kind of fashionable dress can be said to be different for everyone, making people secretly exclaim "Good!"

In addition, the red leaves are really intoxicatingly red. Many people sit under the mountain peaks full of red leaves drinking, and their faces are as red as the red leaves. I love Paris, the intoxicating Paris!)

The above is my impression after reading A Woman's Confession.

As for the other articles, except for (Urban Fantasia), which is a different kind of symbolic style, unseen in the author's works, they all have one thing in common, that is, they can contain a deep sadness in the plain narration, that is, the sentence-making and wording have no traces of chiseling. The author is a prolific writer. In the past two years, four collections of creations and eight children's literature works have been published. It is true as the author himself said, (If I stay in Shanghai again, I am afraid that I will write a lot of books,) but the unique color in his works is unintentional, unpretentious, and full of the unrestrained beauty like idle clouds and wild cranes, which can be found everywhere. In short, these works are not novels made up, but novels written out. This may be one of his characteristics.

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational...etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books and newspapers are not introduced.

(2) The pictures are limited to the latest works of new writers at home and abroad and related illustrations related to the text.

(3) We regret that we cannot publish texts on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books.

Social News

Marshal Foch's European War Diary

— Translated by Gu Angruo

The battle to clear the remnants of the enemy north of the 疴亚斯 River has now been completely successful. Before concentrating our forces to advance on Cambrai and Mezières, we must first conduct the battle of the Meuse River according to the planned plan, with a large American force as a reserve. I then replied to Admiral Haig,

...The final objective you mentioned in your letter coincides with my plan for the Allied forces to fight. These battles are being conducted separately in several different areas. The time between each battle is very short. Now we only need to actively develop these battles. I am focusing on achieving this goal.

The allocation of all forces now must depend on the outcome of future battles. It is also the same whether American troops still need to be transferred to the British side. We can only push forward with all our strength for the time being.

On August 26, Commander Horne directed the British right wing to attack east of Arras, winning a great victory in one battle. The next day, he seized the ferry crossing of the Saint-Cyr River under Clercy. On the 28th, he captured Clercy and attacked the Telequancian line. This is the enemy's base. The enemy defended by danger, and it was difficult for our army to advance again. On the 29th, the enemy took advantage of its position to counterattack the British First Army. Although unsuccessful, the enemy seized the opportunity to retreat further south.

The German army, seeing Commander Horne's rapid advance and the threat of the British Third and Fourth Armies and the French First Army, was greatly frightened. It immediately carried out a retreat along the vast line between the Saint-Cyr River and the 疴亚斯 River on August 27, 28, and 29, deploying defenses on the Cham River and the North Canal. Key towns such as Combles, Herschnault, La Vacquerie, and Noyon in the middle road were abandoned. On the west bank of the Cham River, the enemy is now defending only a bridgehead in front of Péronne. Our army must defeat the enemy here with a main force attack.

On August 30, the British Fourth Army seized the railway bridge south of the city. On the night of August 31 and September 1, it occupied the key of the city of Péronne's defense, the Little Mountain of Saint-Quentin. At dawn the next day, the German army in the ancient city of Péronne surrendered.

The British First Army continued to advance on the extreme left wing of the battle line, preparing to attack the Telequancian line. The British-French central army (British Third, Fourth Armies, French First, Third Armies) was attacking the Cham River line. The French Tenth Army was on the right wing of the battle line, fighting fiercely on the plateau north of Soissons between the Aisne River and the Ailette River. The enemy defended by danger and trenches. Mount Saint-Pépin was the pillar of the German defense for four years and would not be easily abandoned. However, the French Tenth Army advanced inch by inch, progressing daily, and finally captured the heights of Celles-sur-Aisne on September 2 and reached the highway from Soissons to the Celles-sur-Aisne villa area.

At the other end of the battle line, the British First Army re-attacked. After fierce fighting on September 2, it broke through the Telequancian line and advanced several miles towards Marquion. The enemy suffered a heavy blow and retreated along the entire line between the Cham River and the Saint-Cyr River, deploying a new defense line before the Hindenburg Line, relying on the Tortille River and the North Canal.

In this way, after the failure of the German offensive on July 15, the Allied forces quickly took the opportunity to counterattack and won a great victory. The goals in the plan of July 24 have now been fully achieved. On July 18, the reserve group army (Sixth, Tenth Armies) attacked between the Aisne River and the Marne River. Soon, the central group army (Ninth, Fifth Armies) continued to advance between the Marne River and the Vesle River. Within three weeks, the enemy was driven back to the Vesle River, and the Paris-Châlons-sur-Marne railway line was cleared.

On August 8, the French and British armies attacked between the Ancre River and the Avre River. Within three days, the enemy retreated to the old defense line of 1914, and the Amiens and Paris-Amiens railway lines were completely out of danger.

After these goals were achieved, the British First, Third, Fourth Armies and the French First, Third, Thirteenth Armies simultaneously attacked the entire line between Arras and Soissons. After two weeks of fierce fighting, the enemy was greatly shaken and retreated to the Hindenburg Line. (To be continued)

Social News Manuscript Guidelines

(1) The text is about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas

(2) Hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life and other news. The pictures are limited to lyrical expression about social life in various forms.
